Utah Code Annotated - Title 61 - Securities Division - Real Estate Division
===========================================================================

Utah Code Annotated - Title 61 - Chapter 1 - Utah Uniform Securities Act
************************************************************************

Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-1 Fraud unlawful.
--------------------------------------------
It is unlawful for any person, in connection with the offer, sale, or purchase of any security, directly or indirectly to:Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-1(1): employ any device, scheme, or artifice to defraud;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-1(2): make any untrue statement of a material fact or to omit to state a material fact necessary in order to make the statements made, in the light of the circumstances under which they are made, not misleading; or
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-1(3): engage in any act, practice, or course of business which operates or would operate as a fraud or deceit upon any person.


Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-2 Investment adviser -- Unlawful acts.
-----------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-2(1): It is unlawful for any person who receives any consideration from another person primarily for advising the other person as to the value of securities or their purchase or sale, whether through the issuance of analyses or reports or otherwise to:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-2(1)(a): employ any device, scheme, or artifice to defraud the other person;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-2(1)(b): engage in any act, practice, or course of business which operates or would operate as a fraud or deceit upon the other person; or
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-2(1)(c): divide or otherwise split any consideration with any person not licensed under this chapter as an investment adviser or investment adviser representative.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-2(2): 61-1-2(2)(a)(i); 61-1-2(2)(a)(ii)
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-2(2)(a): Except as may be permitted by rule of the division, it is unlawful for any investment adviser to enter into, extend, or renew any investment advisory contract unless it provides in writing that:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-2(2)(a)(i): the investment adviser shall not be compensated on the basis of a share of capital gains upon or capital appreciation of the funds or any portion of the funds of the client;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-2(2)(a)(ii): no assignment of the contract may be made by the investment adviser without the consent of the other party to the contract; and
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-2(2)(a)(iii): the investment adviser, if a partnership, shall notify the other party to the contract of any change in the membership of the partnership within a reasonable time after the change.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-2(2)(b): 61-1-2(2)(a)(i) Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-2(2)(c): 61-1-2(2)(a)(ii) "Assignment," as used in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-2(2)(d): If the investment adviser is a partnership, no assignment of an investment advisory contract is considered to result from the death or withdrawal of a minority of the members of the investment adviser having only a minority interest in the business of the investment adviser, or from the admission to the investment adviser of one or more members who, after admission, will be only a minority of the members and will have only a minority interest in the business.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-2(3): It is unlawful for any investment adviser to take or have custody of any securities or funds of any client if:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-2(3)(a): the division by rule prohibits custody; or
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-2(3)(b): in the absence of a rule, the investment adviser fails to notify the division that he has or may have custody.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-2(4): 61-1-2(2)(a)(i); (ii); (iii) The division may by rule adopt exemptions from Subsections


Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-3 Licensing of broker-dealers, agents, investment advisers, and investment adviser representatives.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-3(1): It is unlawful for a person to transact business in this state as a broker-dealer or agent unless the person is licensed under this chapter.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-3(2): (2)(d)(i)(A); (2)(d); (2)(d)(i)
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-3(2)(a): 
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-3(2)(a)(i): It is unlawful for a broker-dealer or issuer to employ or engage an agent unless the agent is licensed.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-3(2)(a)(ii): The license of an agent is not effective during any period when the agent is not associated with:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-3(2)(a)(ii)(A): a particular broker-dealer licensed under this chapter; or
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-3(2)(a)(ii)(B): a particular issuer.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-3(2)(b): When an agent begins or terminates an association with a broker-dealer or issuer, or begins or terminates activities as an agent, the agent and the broker-dealer or issuer shall promptly notify the division.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-3(2)(c): An agent who terminates an association with a broker-dealer or issuer is considered to be unlicensed until the day on which the division:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-3(2)(c)(i): approves the agent's association with a different broker-dealer or issuer; and
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-3(2)(c)(ii): notifies the agent of the division's approval of the association.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-3(2)(d): (2)(d)(i)(A); (2)(d); (2)(d)(i)
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-3(2)(d)(i): (2)(d)(i)(A) It is unlawful for a broker-dealer or an issuer engaged, directly or indirectly, in offering, offering to purchase, purchasing, or selling a security in this state, to employ or associate with an individual to engage in an activity related to a securities transaction in this state if:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-3(2)(d)(i)(A): 
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-3(2)(d)(i)(A)(I): the license of the individual is suspended or revoked; or
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-3(2)(d)(i)(A)(II): the individual is barred from employment or association with a broker-dealer, an issuer, or a state or federal covered investment adviser; and
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-3(2)(d)(i)(B): (2)(d)(i)(A) the suspension, revocation, or bar described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-3(2)(d)(i)(B)(I): under this chapter;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-3(2)(d)(i)(B)(II): of the Securities and Exchange Commission;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-3(2)(d)(i)(B)(III): of a self-regulatory organization; or
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-3(2)(d)(i)(B)(IV): of a securities administrator of a state other than Utah.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-3(2)(d)(ii): (2)(d) A broker-dealer or issuer does not violate this Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-3(2)(d)(iii): (2)(d)(i) An order under this chapter may modify or waive, in whole or in part, the application of Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-3(3): (3)(b) It is unlawful for a person to transact business in this state as an investment adviser or as an investment adviser representative unless:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-3(3)(a): the person is licensed under this chapter;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-3(3)(b): the person's only clients in this state are:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-3(3)(b)(i): one or more of the following whether acting for itself or as a trustee with investment control:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-3(3)(b)(i)(A): an investment company as defined in the Investment Company Act of 1940;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-3(3)(b)(i)(B): another investment adviser;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-3(3)(b)(i)(C): a federal covered adviser;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-3(3)(b)(i)(D): a broker-dealer;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-3(3)(b)(i)(E): a depository institution;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-3(3)(b)(i)(F): a trust company;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-3(3)(b)(i)(G): an insurance company;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-3(3)(b)(i)(H): an employee benefit plan with assets of not less than $1,000,000; or
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-3(3)(b)(i)(I): a governmental agency or instrumentality; or
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-3(3)(b)(ii): other institutional investors as are designated by rule or order of the director; or
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-3(3)(c): (3)(b) the person:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-3(3)(c)(i): 
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-3(3)(c)(i)(A): is licensed in another state as an investment adviser or an investment adviser representative; or
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-3(3)(c)(i)(B): is exempt from licensing under Section 222(d) of the Investment Advisers Act of 1940;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-3(3)(c)(ii): has no place of business in this state; and
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-3(3)(c)(iii): (3)(b) during the preceding 12-month period has had not more than five clients, other than those specified in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-3(4): Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act; (3) It is unlawful for a person to hold oneself out as a provider of investment advice or as a provider of investment advisory services or otherwise represent that the person is a financial planner, financial adviser, financial consultant, or holds any other similar title as the division may specify in rule made in accordance with
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-3(4)(a): the person is a federal covered adviser;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-3(4)(b): (3) it is lawful for the person to transact business in this state as an investment adviser or as an investment adviser representative under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-3(4)(c): the person:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-3(4)(c)(i): is not an investment adviser or an investment adviser representative; and
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-3(4)(c)(ii): is otherwise licensed under this chapter to transact business in the state.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-3(5): (5)(a)(iii); (5)(a)(iii)
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-3(5)(a): It is unlawful for:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-3(5)(a)(i): a person required to be licensed as an investment adviser under this chapter to employ an investment adviser representative unless the investment adviser representative is licensed under this chapter, except that the license of an investment adviser representative is not effective during any period when the person is not employed by an investment adviser licensed under this chapter;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-3(5)(a)(ii): a federal covered adviser to employ, supervise, or associate with an investment adviser representative having a place of business located in this state, unless the investment adviser representative is:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-3(5)(a)(ii)(A): licensed under this chapter; or
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-3(5)(a)(ii)(B): exempt from licensing; or
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-3(5)(a)(iii): an investment adviser, directly or indirectly, to employ or associate with an individual to engage in an activity related to providing investment advice in this state if:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-3(5)(a)(iii)(A): 
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-3(5)(a)(iii)(A)(I): the license of the individual is suspended or revoked; or
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-3(5)(a)(iii)(A)(II): the individual is barred from employment or association with a state or federal covered investment adviser, broker-dealer, or issuer; and
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-3(5)(a)(iii)(B): the suspension, revocation, or bar is by an order:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-3(5)(a)(iii)(B)(I): under this chapter;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-3(5)(a)(iii)(B)(II): of the Securities and Exchange Commission;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-3(5)(a)(iii)(B)(III): a self-regulatory organization; or
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-3(5)(a)(iii)(B)(IV): a securities administrator of a state other than Utah.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-3(5)(b): (5)(a)(iii); (5)(a)(iii)
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-3(5)(b)(i): (5)(a)(iii) An investment adviser does not violate Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-3(5)(b)(ii): (5)(a)(iii) An order under this chapter may waive, in whole or in part, the application of Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-3(5)(c): When an investment adviser representative required to be licensed under this chapter begins or terminates employment with an investment adviser, the investment adviser shall promptly notify the division.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-3(5)(d): An investment adviser representative who terminates association with an investment adviser is considered unlicensed until the day on which the division:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-3(5)(d)(i): approves the investment adviser representative's association with a different investment adviser; and
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-3(5)(d)(ii): notifies the investment adviser representative of the division's approval of the association.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-3(6): (3)(b); (3)(c)(iii); 61-1-4 Except with respect to an investment adviser whose only clients are those described under Subsections


Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-4 Licensing and notice filing procedure.
-------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-4(1): 61-1-26; 63G-2-302(1)(i); 61-1-6; Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act; (1)(e)(v)(A)
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-4(1)(a): 61-1-26 A broker-dealer, agent, investment adviser, or investment adviser representative shall obtain an initial or renewal license by filing with the division or its designee an application together with a consent to service of process under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-4(1)(b): 63G-2-302(1)(i)
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-4(1)(b)(i): The application shall contain the applicant's Social Security number and whatever information the division by rule requires concerning such matters as:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-4(1)(b)(i)(A): the applicant's form and place of organization;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-4(1)(b)(i)(B): the applicant's proposed method of doing business;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-4(1)(b)(i)(C): 
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-4(1)(b)(i)(C)(I): the qualifications and business history of the applicant; and
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-4(1)(b)(i)(C)(II): in the case of a broker-dealer or investment adviser, the qualifications and business history of any partner, officer, or director, any person occupying a similar status or performing similar functions, or any person directly or indirectly controlling the broker-dealer or investment adviser;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-4(1)(b)(i)(D): whether the applicant has been subject to:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-4(1)(b)(i)(D)(I): an injunction, administrative order, or misdemeanor conviction involving a security or any aspect of the securities business; or
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-4(1)(b)(i)(D)(II): a felony conviction; and
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-4(1)(b)(i)(E): the applicant's financial condition and history.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-4(1)(b)(ii): 63G-2-302(1)(i) An applicant's Social Security number is a private record under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-4(1)(c): The division may, by rule or order, require an applicant for an initial license to publish an announcement of the application in one or more specified newspapers published in this state.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-4(1)(d): A license or notice filing of a broker-dealer, agent, investment adviser, or investment adviser representative expires on December 31 of each year.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-4(1)(e): 61-1-6; Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act; (1)(e)(v)(A)
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-4(1)(e)(i): 61-1-6 If no denial order is in effect and no proceeding is pending under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-4(1)(e)(ii): The division may by rule or order specify an earlier effective date and may by order defer the effective date until noon of the 30th day after the filing of any amendment.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-4(1)(e)(iii): Licensing of a broker-dealer automatically constitutes licensing of only one partner, officer, director, or a person occupying a similar status or performing similar functions as a licensed agent of the broker-dealer.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-4(1)(e)(iv): Licensing of an investment adviser automatically constitutes licensing of only one partner, officer, director, or a person occupying a similar status or performing similar functions.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-4(1)(e)(v): Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act; (1)(e)(v)(A)
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-4(1)(e)(v)(A): For purposes of the activities of a licensee in this state, during the time period that a broker-dealer or investment adviser is licensed in this state:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-4(1)(e)(v)(A)(I): the broker-dealer shall maintain a principal; and
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-4(1)(e)(v)(A)(II): the investment adviser shall maintain a designated official.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-4(1)(e)(v)(B): Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act The division may by rule made in accordance with
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-4(1)(e)(v)(B)(I): a principal or designated official at the time a license is issued; and
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-4(1)(e)(v)(B)(II): a different principal or designated official if:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-4(1)(e)(v)(B)(II)(Aa): a broker-dealer changes its principal; or
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-4(1)(e)(v)(B)(II)(Bb): an investment adviser changes its designated official.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-4(1)(e)(v)(C): (1)(e)(v)(A) A principal or designated official identified in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-4(2): 61-1-3(3)(b); (3)(c)(iii) Except with respect to a federal covered adviser whose only clients are those described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-4(3): 61-1-18.4; 61-1-18.4; 61-1-18.4
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-4(3)(a): 61-1-18.4 An applicant for an initial or renewal license as a broker-dealer or agent shall pay a reasonable filing fee as determined under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-4(3)(b): 61-1-18.4 An applicant for an initial or renewal license as an investment adviser or investment adviser representative who is subject to licensing under this chapter shall pay a reasonable filing fee as determined under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-4(3)(c): 61-1-18.4 A person acting as a federal covered adviser in this state shall pay an initial and renewal notice filing fee as determined under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-4(3)(d): If the license or renewal is not granted or the application is withdrawn, the division shall retain the fee.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-4(4): A licensed broker-dealer or investment adviser may file an application for licensing of a successor for the unexpired portion of the year.  There shall be no filing fee.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-4(5): The division may by rule or order:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-4(5)(a): require a minimum capital for a licensed broker-dealer, subject to the limitations of Section 15 of the Securities Exchange Act of 1934; and
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-4(5)(b): establish minimum financial requirements for an investment adviser:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-4(5)(b)(i): subject to the limitations of Section 222 of the Investment Advisers Act of 1940; and
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-4(5)(b)(ii): which may include different requirements for an investment adviser who maintains custody of or has discretionary authority over client funds or securities and an investment adviser who does not.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-4(6): 61-1-22
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-4(6)(a): The division may by rule or order require a licensed broker-dealer or investment adviser who has custody of or discretionary authority over client funds or securities to post one or more bonds in amounts and under conditions as the division may prescribe, subject to the limitations of Section 15 of the Securities Exchange Act of 1934 for a broker-dealer, and Section 222 of the Investment Advisers Act of 1940 for an investment adviser.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-4(6)(b): An appropriate deposit of cash or securities may be accepted in lieu of a required bond.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-4(6)(c): A bond may not be required of a licensee whose net capital, or in the case of an investment adviser whose minimum financial requirements, which may be defined by rule, exceeds the amounts required by the division.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-4(6)(d): 61-1-22 A bond shall provide for suit on the bond by a person who has a cause of action under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-4(6)(e): A bond shall provide that a suit may not be maintained to enforce liability on the bond unless brought before the earlier of:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-4(6)(e)(i): the expiration of five years after the act or transaction constituting the violation; or
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-4(6)(e)(ii): the expiration of two years after the discovery by the plaintiff of the facts constituting the violation.


Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-5 Postlicensing provisions.
------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-5(1): 
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-5(1)(a): A licensed broker-dealer and investment adviser shall make and keep such accounts, correspondence, memoranda, papers, books, and other records as the division by rule prescribes, except as provided in:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-5(1)(a)(i): Section 15 of the Securities Exchange Act of 1934 in the case of a broker-dealer; and
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-5(1)(a)(ii): Section 222 of the Investment Advisers Act of 1940 in the case of an investment adviser.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-5(1)(b): A record required to be made and kept by an investment adviser shall be preserved for the period as the division prescribes by rule or order.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-5(2): 
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-5(2)(a): A licensed broker-dealer shall, within 24 hours after demand, furnish to any customer or principal for whom the broker-dealer has executed any order for the purchase or sale of any securities, either for immediate or future delivery, a written statement showing:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-5(2)(a)(i): the time when the securities were bought and sold;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-5(2)(a)(ii): the place where the securities were bought and sold; and
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-5(2)(a)(iii): the price at which the securities were bought and sold.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-5(2)(b): With respect to investment advisers, the division may require that certain information be furnished or disseminated as necessary or appropriate in the public interest or for the protection of investors and advisory clients.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-5(2)(c): To the extent determined by the director, information furnished to clients or prospective clients of an investment adviser who would be in compliance with the Investment Advisers Act of 1940 and the rules under the Investment Advisers Act of 1940 may be considered to satisfy this requirement.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-5(3): A licensed broker-dealer and investment adviser shall file financial reports as the division by rule prescribes, except as provided in:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-5(3)(a): Section 15 of the Securities Exchange Act of 1934 in the case of a broker-dealer; and
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-5(3)(b): Section 222 of the Investment Advisers Act of 1940 in the case of an investment adviser.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-5(4): 61-1-3 If the information contained in any document filed with the division is or becomes inaccurate or incomplete in any material respect, the licensee or federal covered adviser shall promptly file a correcting amendment if the document is filed with respect to a licensee, or when such amendment is required to be filed with the Securities and Exchange Commission if the document is filed with respect to a federal covered adviser, unless notification of the correction has been given under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-5(5): (1)
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-5(5)(a): (1) A record referred to in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-5(5)(b): For the purpose of avoiding unnecessary duplication of examination, the division may cooperate with:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-5(5)(b)(i): the securities administrators of other states;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-5(5)(b)(ii): the Securities and Exchange Commission; and
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-5(5)(b)(iii): national securities exchanges or national securities associations registered under the Securities Exchange Act of 1934.


Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-6 Sanctions.
---------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-6(1): Title 63G, Chapter 4, Administrative Procedures Act; 61-1-31; (1)(a) Subject to the other provisions of this section and by means of an adjudicative proceeding conducted in accordance with
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-6(1)(a): 61-1-31; (1)(a) the commission may issue an order:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-6(1)(a)(i): suspending or revoking a license;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-6(1)(a)(ii): barring or censuring a licensee or an officer, director, partner, or person occupying a similar status or performing similar functions for a licensee from employment with a licensed broker-dealer or investment adviser;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-6(1)(a)(iii): restricting or limiting a licensee as to a function or activity of the business for which a license is required in this state;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-6(1)(a)(iv): 61-1-31 imposing a fine in an amount determined after considering the factors set forth in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-6(1)(a)(v): requiring disgorgement;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-6(1)(a)(vi): requiring restitution;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-6(1)(a)(vii): requiring rescission; or
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-6(1)(a)(viii): (1)(a) taking any combination of actions under this Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-6(1)(b): the director may deny a license.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-6(2): (1)(a); (1)(b); (2)(b); (2)(a)(ii)(H); (5); (2)(c); (2)(a)(ii)(D); (2)(a)(ii)(F); (2)(a)(ii)(F); (2)(a)(ii)(L); (1); (2)(a)(ii)(L)
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-6(2)(a): (1)(a); (1)(b); (2)(b); (2)(a)(ii)(H); (5); (2)(c); (2)(a)(ii)(D) The commission may impose a sanction in accordance with Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-6(2)(a)(i): that it is in the public interest; and
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-6(2)(a)(ii): (2)(b); (2)(a)(ii)(H); (5); (2)(c); (2)(a)(ii)(D) with respect to the applicant or licensee or, in the case of a broker-dealer or investment adviser, a partner, officer, or director, or a person occupying a similar status or performing similar functions, or a person directly or indirectly controlling the broker-dealer or investment adviser, that the person:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-6(2)(a)(ii)(A): has filed an application for a license that, as of the effective date of the application or as of any date after filing in the case of an order denying effectiveness:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-6(2)(a)(ii)(A)(I): was incomplete in a material respect; or
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-6(2)(a)(ii)(A)(II): contained a statement that was, in light of the circumstances under which it was made, false or misleading with respect to a material fact;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-6(2)(a)(ii)(B): has willfully violated or willfully failed to comply with this chapter or a predecessor act or a rule or order under this chapter or a predecessor act;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-6(2)(a)(ii)(C): was convicted of, or entered a plea of guilty, a plea of no contest, a plea in abeyance, or a similar plea of guilty to:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-6(2)(a)(ii)(C)(I): a misdemeanor involving:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-6(2)(a)(ii)(C)(I)(Aa): fraud or dishonesty; or
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-6(2)(a)(ii)(C)(I)(Bb): a security or any aspect of the securities business; or
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-6(2)(a)(ii)(C)(II): a felony;

Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-6.5 Court-ordered discipline.
--------------------------------------------------------
The division shall promptly withhold, suspend, restrict, or reinstate the use of a license issued under this chapter if so ordered by a court.

Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-7 Registration before sale.
------------------------------------------------------
It is unlawful for any person to offer or sell any security in this state unless it is registered under this chapter, the security or transaction is exempted under Section

Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-9 Registration by coordination.
----------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-9(1): A security for which a registration statement is filed under the Securities Act of 1933 in connection with the same offering may be registered by coordination.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-9(2): 61-1-11(3); 61-1-26 A registration statement under this section shall contain the following information and be accompanied by the following documents in addition to the information specified in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-9(2)(a): one copy of the disclosure statement together with all its amendments filed under the Securities Act of 1933;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-9(2)(b): if the division by rule or otherwise requires:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-9(2)(b)(i): a copy of the articles of incorporation and bylaws or their substantial equivalents currently in effect;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-9(2)(b)(ii): a copy of any agreements with or among underwriters;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-9(2)(b)(iii): a copy of any indenture or other instrument governing the issuance of the security to be registered; and
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-9(2)(b)(iv): a specimen or copy of the security;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-9(2)(c): if the division requests, any other information, or copies of any other documents, filed under the Securities Act of 1933; and
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-9(2)(d): an undertaking to forward all future amendments to the disclosure statement promptly and in any event not later than the first working day after the day they are forwarded to or filed with the Securities and Exchange Commission, whichever first occurs.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-9(3): 61-1-12 A registration statement under this section automatically becomes effective at the moment the disclosure statement becomes effective if all the following conditions are satisfied:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-9(3)(a): 61-1-12 no stop order is in effect and no proceeding is pending under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-9(3)(b): the disclosure statement is on file with the division for at least 20 working days; and
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-9(3)(c): a statement of the maximum and minimum proposed offering prices and the maximum underwriting discounts and commissions is on file for two full working days or such shorter period as the division permits by rule or otherwise and the offering is made within those limitations.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-9(4): 
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-9(4)(a): A registrant shall promptly:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-9(4)(a)(i): notify the division in a record of the date and time when the disclosure statement became effective and the content of the price amendment, if any; and
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-9(4)(a)(ii): file a posteffective amendment containing the information and documents in the price amendment.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-9(4)(b): "Price amendment" means the final federal amendment that includes a statement of the:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-9(4)(b)(i): offering price;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-9(4)(b)(ii): underwriting and selling discounts or commissions;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-9(4)(b)(iii): amount of proceeds;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-9(4)(b)(iv): conversion rates;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-9(4)(b)(v): call prices; and
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-9(4)(b)(vi): other matters dependent upon the offering price.

Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-9(5)(b): (4) If the registrant proves compliance with the requirements of Subsection

Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-10(1): Application may be made to register any security by qualification.

Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-10(2)(a): with respect to the issuer and any significant subsidiary:

Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-10(2)(b)(i): his name, address, and principal occupation for the past five years;

Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-10(2)(b)(iv): a description of any material interest in any material transaction with the issuer or any significant subsidiary affected within the past three years or proposed to be affected;

Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-10(2)(g): the capitalization and long-term debt, on both a current and pro forma basis, of the issuer and any significant subsidiary, including a description of each security outstanding or being registered or otherwise offered, and a statement of the amount and kind of consideration, whether in the form of cash, physical assets, services, patents, goodwill, or anything else, for which the issuer or any subsidiary has issued any of its securities within the past two years or is obligated to issue any of its securities;

Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-10(2)(h)(i): the kind and amount of securities to be offered;

Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-10(2)(h)(iii): any variation therefrom at which any proportion of the offering is to be made to any person or class of persons other than the underwriters, with a specification of any such person or class;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-10(2)(h)(iv): the basis upon which the offering is to be made if otherwise than for cash;

Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-10(2)(i)(iii): the amount to be used for each purpose;

Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-10(2)(i)(v): the amounts of any funds to be raised from other sources to achieve the purposes stated and the sources of any such funds; and
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-10(2)(i)(vi): if any part of the proceeds is to be used to acquire any property, including goodwill, otherwise than in the ordinary course of business, the names and addresses of the vendors, the purchase price, the names of any persons who have received commissions in connection with the acquisition, and the amounts of any such commissions and any other expense in connection with the acquisition, including the cost of borrowing money to finance the acquisition;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-10(2)(j): (2)(b); (d); (e); (f); (h) a description of any stock options or other security options outstanding, or to be created in connection with the offering, together with the amount of any such option held or to be held by every person required to be named in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-10(2)(k): 
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-10(2)(k)(i): the dates of, parties to, and general effect concisely stated of, every management or other material contract made or to be made otherwise than in the ordinary course of business if it is to be performed in whole or in part at or after the filing of the registration statement or was made within the past two years, together with a copy of every such contract; and

Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-10(2)(n): a signed or conformed copy of an opinion of counsel as to the legality of the security being registered, with an English translation if it is in a foreign language, which shall state whether the security when sold will be legally issued, fully paid, and nonassessable, and if a debt security, a binding obligation of the issuer;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-10(2)(o): the written consent of any accountant, engineer, appraiser, or other person whose profession gives authority to a statement made by him, if that person is named as having prepared or certified a report or valuation, other than a public and official document or statement, which is used in connection with the registration statement;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-10(2)(p): 
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-10(2)(p)(i): a balance sheet of the issuer as of a date within four months prior to the filing of the registration statement;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-10(2)(p)(ii): a profit and loss statement and analysis of retained earnings for each of the three fiscal years preceding the date of the balance sheet and for any period between the close of the last fiscal year and the date of the balance sheet, or for the period of the issuer's and any predecessors' existence if less than three years; and
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-10(2)(p)(iii): if any part of the proceeds of the offering is to be applied to the purchase of any business, the same financial statements which would be required if that business were the registrant; and
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-10(2)(q): such additional information or verification of any statement as the division requires by rule or order.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-10(3): A registration statement under this section becomes effective when the division so orders.

Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-10(4)(a): the first written offer made to the person, otherwise than by means of a public advertisement, by or for the account of the issuer or any other person on whose behalf the offering is being made, or by any underwriter or broker-dealer who is offering part of an unsold allotment or subscription taken by the person as a participant in the distribution;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-10(4)(b): the confirmation of any sale made by or for the account of any such person;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-10(4)(c): payment pursuant to any such sale; or
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-10(4)(d): delivery of the security pursuant to any such sale, whichever occurs first.


Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-11 Provisions applicable to registration generally.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-11(1): A registration statement may be filed by the issuer, another person on whose behalf the offering is to be made, or a licensed broker-dealer.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-11(2): 61-1-18.4 A person filing a registration statement shall pay a filing fee as determined under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-11(3): A registration statement shall specify:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-11(3)(a): the amount of securities to be offered in this state;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-11(3)(b): the states in which a registration statement or similar document in connection with the offering is or is to be filed; and
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-11(3)(c): an adverse order, judgment, or decree entered in connection with the offering by the regulatory authorities in each state or by a court or the Securities and Exchange Commission.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-11(4): A document filed under this chapter or a predecessor act within five years preceding the filing of a registration statement may be incorporated by reference in the registration statement to the extent that the document is currently accurate.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-11(5): The division may permit the omission of an item of information or document from a registration statement.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-11(6): (9); 61-1-10 In the case of a nonissuer distribution, information may not be required under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-11(7): (7)
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-11(7)(a): The division may require as a condition of registration by qualification or coordination:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-11(7)(a)(i): that security issued within the past three years or to be issued to a promoter for a consideration substantially different from the public offering price, or to a person for a consideration other than cash, be deposited in escrow; and
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-11(7)(a)(ii): that the proceeds from the sale of the registered security be impounded until the issuer receives a specified amount from the sale of the security either in this state or elsewhere.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-11(7)(b): (7) The division may determine the conditions of an escrow or impounding required by this Subsection

Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-13(1)(f)(i): an agricultural, grain, or livestock product or byproduct, except real property or a timber, agricultural, or livestock product grown or raised on real property and offered or sold by the owner or lessee of the real property;

Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-13(1)(g): 
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-13(1)(g)(i): "Commodity contract" means an account, agreement, or contract for the purchase or sale, primarily for speculation or investment purposes and not for use or consumption by the offeree or purchaser, of one or more commodities, whether for immediate or subsequent delivery or whether delivery is intended by the parties, and whether characterized as a cash contract, deferred shipment or deferred delivery contract, forward contract, futures contract, installment or margin contract, leverage contract, or otherwise.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-13(1)(g)(ii): A commodity contract offered or sold shall, in the absence of evidence to the contrary, be presumed to be offered or sold for speculation or investment purposes.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-13(1)(g)(iii): 
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-13(1)(g)(iii)(A): A commodity contract may not include a contract or agreement that requires, and under which the purchaser receives, within 28 calendar days from the payment in good funds any portion of the purchase price, physical delivery of the total amount of each commodity to be purchased under the contract or agreement.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-13(1)(g)(iii)(B): A purchaser is not considered to have received physical delivery of the total amount of each commodity to be purchased under the contract or agreement when the commodity or commodities are held as collateral for a loan or are subject to a lien of any person when the loan or lien arises in connection with the purchase of each commodity or commodities.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-13(1)(h): 
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-13(1)(h)(i): "Commodity option" means an account, agreement, or contract giving a party to the option the right but not the obligation to purchase or sell one or more commodities or one or more commodity contracts, or both whether characterized as an option, privilege, indemnity, bid, offer, put, call, advance guaranty, decline guaranty, or otherwise.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-13(1)(h)(ii): "Commodity option" does not include an option traded on a national securities exchange registered:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-13(1)(h)(ii)(A): with the Securities and Exchange Commission; or
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-13(1)(h)(ii)(B): on a board of trade designated as a contract market by the Commodity Futures Trading Commission.

Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-13(1)(u): 
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-13(1)(u)(i): "Issuer" means a person who issues or proposes to issue a security or has outstanding a security that it has issued.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-13(1)(u)(ii): With respect to a preorganization certificate or subscription, "issuer" means the one or more promoters of the person to be organized.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-13(1)(u)(iii): "Issuer" means the one or more persons performing the acts and assuming duties of a depositor or manager under the provisions of the trust or other agreement or instrument under which the security is issued with respect to:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-13(1)(u)(iii)(A): interests in trusts, including collateral trust certificates, voting trust certificates, and certificates of deposit for securities; or
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-13(1)(u)(iii)(B): shares in an investment company without a board of directors.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-13(1)(u)(iv): With respect to an equipment trust certificate, a conditional sales contract, or similar securities serving the same purpose, "issuer" means the person by whom the equipment or property is to be used.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-13(1)(u)(v): With respect to interests in partnerships, general or limited, "issuer" means the partnership itself and not the general partner or partners.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-13(1)(u)(vi): With respect to certificates of interest or participation in oil, gas, or mining titles or leases or in payment out of production under the titles or leases, "issuer" means the owner of the title or lease or right of production, whether whole or fractional, who creates fractional interests therein for the purpose of sale.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-13(1)(v):

Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-13(1)(v)(i)(B): the death benefit under a policy.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-13(1)(v)(ii): "Life settlement interest" does not include the initial purchase from the owner by a life settlement provider.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-13(1)(w): "Nonissuer" means not directly or indirectly for the benefit of the issuer.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-13(1)(x): "Person" means:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-13(1)(x)(i): an individual;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-13(1)(x)(ii): a corporation;

Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-16 False statements unlawful.
--------------------------------------------------------
It is unlawful for a person to make or cause to be made, in any document filed with the division or in any proceeding, examination, or investigation conducted under this chapter, any statement that is, at the time and in the light of the circumstances under which it is made, false or misleading in any material respect.

Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-17 No finding by division on merits -- Contrary representation unlawful.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-17(1): Neither the fact that an application for registration or a registration statement has been filed nor the fact that a person or security is effectively registered constitutes a finding by the division that any document filed under this chapter is true, complete, and not misleading. Neither any such fact nor the fact that an exemption or exception is available for a security or a transaction means that the division has passed in any way upon the merits or qualifications of, or recommended or given approval to, any person, security, or transaction.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-17(2): (1) It is unlawful to make, or cause to be made, to any prospective purchaser, customer, or client any representation inconsistent with Subsection

Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-18.1 Technical experts and specialists -- Employment -- Contracts.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
The director may employ or contract with technical experts and specialists including but not limited to certified public accountants, appraisers, engineers, and tax accountants to conduct or participate in any examination, audit, investigation or proceeding.

Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-18.2 Budget -- Annual report.
--------------------------------------------------------
The director shall annually prepare and submit to the executive director:Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-18.2(1): a budget for the expenses of the division and commission for the administration and enforcement of this chapter for the next fiscal year; and
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-18.2(2): a report outlining the division's and commission's work for the preceding fiscal year.


Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-18.3 Information obtained by division or commission -- Use for personal benefit prohibited -- Disclosure.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-18.3(1): It is unlawful for an employee of the division or a member of the commission to use for personal benefit any non-public information that is filed with or obtained by the division or commission.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-18.3(2): (1) This chapter does not authorize the division, an employee of the division, the commission, or a member of the commission to disclose information described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-18.3(3): No provision of this chapter either creates or derogates from a privilege that exists at common law or otherwise when documentary or other evidence is sought under subpoena directed to:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-18.3(3)(a): the division;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-18.3(3)(b): the commission;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-18.3(3)(c): a member of the commission; or
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-18.3(3)(d): an employee of the division.

Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-19 Investigations authorized.
--------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-19(1): 
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-19(1)(a): The division may make any public or private investigations within or without this state as the division considers necessary to determine whether a person has violated, is violating, or is about to violate this chapter or a rule or order issued under this chapter.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-19(1)(b): To aid in the enforcement of this chapter or in the prescribing of rules and forms issued under this chapter, the division may require or permit a person to file a statement in writing, under oath or otherwise as to all the facts and circumstances concerning the matter to be investigated.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-19(1)(c): The division may publish information concerning a violation of this chapter or the violation of a rule or order issued under this chapter.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-19(2): For the purpose of an investigation or proceeding under this chapter, the division, the commission, or an employee designated by the division may:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-19(2)(a): administer an oath or affirmation;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-19(2)(b): subpoena a witness and compel the attendance of the witness;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-19(2)(c): take evidence; and
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-19(2)(d): require the production of any books, papers, correspondence, memoranda, agreements, or other documents or records  relevant or material to the investigation.


Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-20 Enforcement.
------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-20(1): 61-1-31; (1)(e) Whenever it appears to the director that a person has engaged, is engaging, or is about to engage in an act or practice constituting a violation of this chapter or a rule or order under this chapter, in addition to specific powers granted in this chapter:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-20(1)(a): the director may issue an order directing the person to appear before the commission and show cause why an order should not be issued directing the person to cease and desist from engaging in the act or practice, or doing an act in furtherance of the activity;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-20(1)(b): the order to show cause shall state the reasons for the order and the date of the hearing;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-20(1)(c): the director shall promptly serve a copy of the order to show cause upon a person named in the order;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-20(1)(d): the commission shall hold a hearing on the order to show cause no sooner than 10 business days after the order is issued;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-20(1)(e): 61-1-31; (1)(e) after a hearing, the commission may:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-20(1)(e)(i): issue an order to cease and desist from engaging in an act or practice constituting a violation of this chapter or a rule or order under this chapter;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-20(1)(e)(ii): 61-1-31 impose a fine in an amount determined after considering the factors set forth in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-20(1)(e)(iii): order disgorgement;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-20(1)(e)(iv): order restitution;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-20(1)(e)(v): order rescission;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-20(1)(e)(vi): bar or suspend that person from associating with a licensed broker-dealer or investment adviser in this state; and
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-20(1)(e)(vii): (1)(e) impose a combination of sanctions in this Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-20(2): 61-1-31; (2)
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-20(2)(a): The director may bring an action in the appropriate district court of this state or the appropriate court of another state to enjoin an act or practice and to enforce compliance with this chapter or a rule or order under this chapter.

Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-21 Penalties for violations.
-------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-21(1): 61-1-1; 61-1-16; 61-1-16 A person is guilty of a third degree felony who willfully violates:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-21(1)(a): 61-1-1; 61-1-16 a provision of this chapter except Sections
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-21(1)(b): an order issued under this chapter; or
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-21(1)(c): 61-1-16 Section
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-21(2): 61-1-1 Subject to the other provisions of this section, a person who willfully violates Section
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-21(2)(a): is guilty of a third degree felony if, at the time the crime was committed, the property, money, or thing unlawfully obtained or sought to be obtained was worth less than $10,000; or
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-21(2)(b): is guilty of a second degree felony if, at the time the crime was committed, the property, money, or thing unlawfully obtained or sought to be obtained was worth $10,000 or more.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-21(3): 61-1-1 A person who willfully violates Section
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-21(3)(a): at the time the crime was committed, the property, money, or thing unlawfully obtained or sought to be obtained was worth less than $10,000; and
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-21(3)(b): in connection with that violation, the violator knowingly accepted any money representing:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-21(3)(b)(i): equity in a person's primary residence;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-21(3)(b)(ii): a withdrawal from an individual retirement account;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-21(3)(b)(iii): a withdrawal from a qualified retirement plan as defined in the Internal Revenue Code;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-21(3)(b)(iv): an investment by a person over whom the violator exercises undue influence; or
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-21(3)(b)(v): an investment by a person that the violator knows is a vulnerable adult.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-21(4): 61-1-1 A person who willfully violates Section
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-21(4)(a): at the time the crime was committed, the property, money, or thing unlawfully obtained or sought to be obtained was worth $10,000 or more; and
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-21(4)(b): in connection with that violation, the violator knowingly accepted any money representing:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-21(4)(b)(i): equity in a person's primary residence;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-21(4)(b)(ii): a withdrawal from an individual retirement account;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-21(4)(b)(iii): a withdrawal from a qualified retirement plan as defined in the Internal Revenue Code;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-21(4)(b)(iv): an investment by a person over whom the violator exercises undue influence; or
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-21(4)(b)(v): an investment by a person that the violator knows is a vulnerable adult.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-21(5): When amounts of property, money, or other things are unlawfully obtained or sought to be obtained under a series of acts or continuing course of business, whether from the same or several sources, the amounts may be aggregated in determining the level of offense.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-21(6): It is an affirmative defense under this section against a claim that the person violated an order issued under this chapter for the person to prove that the person had no knowledge of the order.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-21(7): 61-1-20(2)(b) In addition to any other penalty for a criminal violation of this chapter, the sentencing judge may impose a penalty or remedy provided for in Subsection


Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-21.1 Limitation of prosecutions.
-----------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-21.1(1): An indictment or information may not be returned or civil complaint filed under this chapter more than five years after the alleged violation.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-21.1(2): An administrative action filed under this chapter may be commenced within 10 years after the violation occurs.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-21.1(3): (1); (2) When a violation is based on a series of acts or continuing course of business, the conduct may be considered as one continuing offense and the period of limitation described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-21.1(4): 76-1-302; Title 78B, Chapter 2, Statutes of Limitations As to causes of action arising from violations of this chapter, the limitation of prosecutions provided in this section supersedes the limitation of actions provided in Section


Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-21.5 Legal counsel -- Prosecutions.
--------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-21.5(1): The attorney general shall advise and represent the division, the commission, and the staff of the division in all civil matters, administrative or judicial, requiring legal counsel or services in:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-21.5(1)(a): the exercise or defense of the division's or commission's power; or
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-21.5(1)(b): the performance of the division's or commission's duties.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-21.5(2): With the concurrence of the attorney general, the staff of the division may represent the division in hearings conducted during the course of adjudicative proceedings of the commission or the division.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-21.5(3): 
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-21.5(3)(a): In the prosecution of all criminal actions under this chapter, the attorney general, county attorney, or district attorney of the appropriate jurisdiction, shall provide all legal services for the division, the commission, and the staff of the division.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-21.5(3)(b): The division or commission may refer evidence that is available concerning a violation of this chapter for criminal prosecution to:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-21.5(3)(b)(i): the attorney general; or
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-21.5(3)(b)(ii): the appropriate county attorney, district attorney, or United States Attorney's Office.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-21.5(4): The attorney general, a county attorney, or a district attorney of the appropriate jurisdiction may institute a criminal proceeding under this chapter, with or without referral from the division.

Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-25(5): The division may issue an interpretative opinion requested by an interested person if the commission concurs in the interpretative opinion.


Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-26 Scope of the act -- Service of process.
---------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-26(1): 61-1-1; 61-1-3(1); 61-1-7; 61-1-15.5; 61-1-17; 61-1-22 Section
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-26(1)(a): an offer to sell is made in this state; or
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-26(1)(b): an offer to buy is made and accepted in this state.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-26(2): 61-1-1; 61-1-3(1); 61-1-17 Section
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-26(2)(a): an offer to buy is made in this state; or
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-26(2)(b): an offer to sell is made and accepted in this state.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-26(3): For the purposes of this section, an offer to sell or to buy is made in this state whether or not either party is then present in this state, when the offer:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-26(3)(a): originates from this state; or
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-26(3)(b): is directed by the offeror to this state and received at the place to which it is directed, or at any post office in this state in the case of a mailed offer.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-26(4): For the purposes of this section, an offer to sell or to buy is accepted in this state when acceptance:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-26(4)(a): is communicated to the offeror in this state; and
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-26(4)(b): has not previously been communicated to the offeror, orally or in writing, outside this state, and acceptance is communicated to the offeror in this state, whether or not either party is then present in this state, when the offeree directs it to the offeror in this state reasonably believing the offeror to be in this state and it is received at the place to which it is directed or at any post office in this state in the case of a mailed acceptance.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-26(5): An offer to sell or to buy is not made in this state when:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-26(5)(a): the publisher circulates or there is circulated on his behalf in this state any bona fide newspaper or other publication of general, regular, and paid circulation which is not published in this state, or which is published in this state but has had more than 2/3 of its circulation outside this state during the past 12 months; or
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-26(5)(b): a radio or television program originating outside this state is received in this state.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-26(6): 61-1-2; 61-1-3(3); 61-1-17 Section
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-26(7): 
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-26(7)(a): Every application for registration under this chapter and every issuer which proposes to offer a security in this state through any person acting on an agency basis in the common-law sense shall file with the division, in such form as it prescribes by rule, an irrevocable consent appointing the division or the director to be his attorney to receive service of any lawful process in any noncriminal suit, action, or proceeding against him or his successor, executor, or administrator which arises under this chapter or any rule or order hereunder after the consent has been filed, with the same force and validity as if served personally on the person filing the consent.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-26(7)(b): A person who has filed such a consent in connection with a previous registration or notice filing need not file another.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-26(7)(c): Service may be made by leaving a copy of the process in the office of the division, but it is not effective unless the plaintiff, who may be the division in a suit, action, or proceeding instituted by it, sends notice of the service and a copy of the process by registered mail to the defendant or respondent at his last address on file with the division, and the plaintiff's affidavit of compliance with this subsection is filed in the case on or before the return day of the process, if any, or within such further time as the court allows.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-26(8): (7)
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-26(8)(a): (7) When any person, including any nonresident of this state, engages in conduct prohibited or made actionable by this chapter or any rule or order hereunder, and he has not filed a consent to service of process under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-26(8)(b): Service may be made by leaving a copy of the process in the office of the division, but it is not effective unless the plaintiff, who may be the division in a suit, action, or proceeding instituted by it, sends notice of the service and a copy of the process by registered mail to the defendant or respondent at his last-known address or takes other steps which are reasonably calculated to give actual notice, and the plaintiff's affidavit of compliance with this subsection is filed in the case on or before the return day of the process, if any, or within such further time as the court allows.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-26(9): When process is served under this section, the court, or the director shall order such continuance as may be necessary to afford the defendant or respondent reasonable opportunity to defend.


Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-27 Construction of chapter.
------------------------------------------------------
This chapter may be so construed as to effectuate its general purpose to make uniform the law of those states which enact it and to coordinate the interpretation and administration of this chapter with the related federal regulation.

Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-28 Citation of chapter.
--------------------------------------------------
This chapter may be cited as the Utah Uniform Securities Act.

Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-29 Savings clause.
---------------------------------------------
If any provision of this chapter or its application to any person or circumstance is held invalid, the invalidity shall not affect other provisions or applications of the chapter which can be given effect without the invalid provision or application.

Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-31 Determining amount of fine.
---------------------------------------------------------
For the purpose of determining the amount of a fine imposed under this chapter, the commission or court shall consider the following factors:Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-31(1): the seriousness, nature, circumstances, extent, and persistence of the conduct constituting the violation;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-31(2): the harm to other persons resulting either directly or indirectly from the violation;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-31(3): 
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-31(3)(a): the cooperation by the person in any inquiry conducted by the division concerning the violation;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-31(3)(b): efforts by the person to prevent future occurrences of the violation; and
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-31(3)(c): efforts by the person to mitigate the harm caused by the violation, including any disgorgement or restitution made to other persons injured by the acts of the person;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-31(4): the history of previous violations by the person;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-31(5): the need to deter the person or other persons from committing the violation in the future;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-31(6): whether the person exercised undue influence;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-31(7): whether the person knew or should have known that the investor was a vulnerable adult;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-31(8): any direct or indirect compensation or economic benefit the person committing the violation received; and
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-31(9): such other matters as justice may require.


Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-32 Exemptions from licensure.
--------------------------------------------------------
Except as otherwise provided by statute or rule, the following individuals may engage in the practice of an occupation or profession regulated by this chapter, subject to the stated circumstances and limitations, without being licensed under this chapter:Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-32(1): an individual licensed under the laws of this state, other than under this chapter, to practice or engage in an occupation or profession, while engaged in the lawful, professional, and competent practice of that occupation or profession;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-32(2): an individual serving in the armed forces of the United States, the United States Public Health Service, the United States Department of Veterans Affairs, or any other federal agency while engaged in activities regulated under this title as a part of employment with that federal agency if the individual holds a valid license to practice the regulated occupation or profession issued by any other state or jurisdiction recognized by the department; and
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-32(3): the spouse of an individual serving in the armed forces of the United States while the individual is stationed within this state, if:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-32(3)(a): the spouse holds a valid license to practice the regulated occupation or profession issued by any other state or jurisdiction recognized by the department; and
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-32(3)(b): the license is current and the spouse is in good standing in the state or jurisdiction of licensure.


Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-101 Title.
-------------------------------------
This part is known as the "Securities Fraud Reporting Program Act."

Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-102 Definitions.
-------------------------------------------
As used in this part:Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-102(1): "Adverse action" means to:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-102(1)(a): discharge, threaten, or directly or indirectly harass an employee; or
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-102(1)(b): otherwise discriminate against an employee in any manner that affects the employee's employment, including:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-102(1)(b)(i): compensation;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-102(1)(b)(ii): terms;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-102(1)(b)(iii): conditions;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-102(1)(b)(iv): location;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-102(1)(b)(v): rights;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-102(1)(b)(vi): immunities;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-102(1)(b)(vii): promotions; or
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-102(1)(b)(viii): privileges.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-102(2): "Covered judicial or administrative action" means a judicial or administrative action brought under this chapter that results in a monetary sanction exceeding $50,000.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-102(3): "Employee" means an individual who performs a service for wages or other remuneration under a contract of hire, written or oral, express or implied.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-102(4): 61-1-18.7 "Fund" means the Securities Investor Education, Training, and Enforcement Fund created in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-102(5): "Original information" means information that is:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-102(5)(a): derived from the independent knowledge or analysis of an individual;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-102(5)(b): not known to the division or commission from a source other than the individual; and
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-102(5)(c): unless the individual is the source of the information, not exclusively derived from:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-102(5)(c)(i): an allegation made in a judicial or administrative hearing;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-102(5)(c)(ii): a government report, hearing, audit, or investigation; or
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-102(5)(c)(iii): the media.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-102(6): "Monetary sanction" means money required to be paid under this chapter as the result of a judicial or administrative action, including a penalty or disgorgement.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-102(7): 61-1-103 "Reporter" means an individual who provides original information relating to a violation in accordance with Section

Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-106 Award for reporter.
--------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-106(1): 61-1-108 Subject to Section
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-106(2): The division shall pay an award under this section from the fund.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-106(3): 
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-106(3)(a): Subject to the other provisions of this section, the commission may determine the amount of award paid under this section, except that in determining the amount the commission shall consider:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-106(3)(a)(i): the significance of the original information provided by the reporter to the success of the covered judicial or administrative action;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-106(3)(a)(ii): the degree of assistance provided by the reporter in relation to the covered judicial or administrative action;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-106(3)(a)(iii): any costs of legal representation for the reporter in relation to the covered judicial or administrative action;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-106(3)(a)(iv): the programmatic interest of the commission in deterring a violation of this chapter by making an award to a reporter who provides original information that leads to the successful enforcement of this chapter;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-106(3)(a)(v): whether, and the extent to which, the reporter or a legal representative of the reporter participated in internal compliance systems, including:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-106(3)(a)(v)(A): whether, and the extent to which, the reporter reported the possible securities violation through internal reporting, legal, or compliance procedures before, or at the same time as reporting the securities violation to the division or commission; and
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-106(3)(a)(v)(B): whether, and the extent to which, the reporter assisted an internal investigation or inquiry concerning the reported securities violation; and
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-106(3)(a)(vi): any other relevant factor that the division may establish by rule.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-106(3)(b): The aggregate amount of awards that the commission may award for a specific covered judicial or administrative action may not exceed:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-106(3)(b)(i): the balance in the fund as of the date the awards are determined; or
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-106(3)(b)(ii): 30%, in total, of what is collected of the monetary sanction imposed in the judicial or administrative action.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-106(4): 61-1-103 The commission may not award a reporter under this section if the reporter:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-106(4)(a): is convicted of a criminal violation related to the covered judicial or administrative action for which the reporter otherwise could receive an award;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-106(4)(b): gains the original information through the performance of an audit of financial statements required under securities laws and for whom providing the original information would violate 15 U.S.C. Sec. 78j-1;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-106(4)(c): 61-1-103 fails to provide the original information to the commission or division in accordance with Section
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-106(4)(d): knowingly or recklessly makes a false, fictitious, or fraudulent statement or misrepresentation;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-106(4)(e): uses a false writing or document knowing that, or with reckless disregard as to whether, the writing or document contains false, fictitious, or fraudulent information;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-106(4)(f): knows that, or has a reckless disregard as to whether, the disclosure is of original information that is false or frivolous;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-106(4)(g): has a legal duty to report the original information to the commission or division; or
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-106(4)(h): qualifies for an award as described in Section 21F of the Securities Exchange Act, 15 U.S.C. Sec. 78u-6, and regulations issued under that section.

------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-201 Definitions.
-------------------------------------------
As used in this part:Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-201(1): 26B-6-201 "Adult Protective Services" means the same as that term is defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-201(2): 26B-6-201 "Eligible adult" means:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-201(2)(a): an individual who is 65 years old or older; or
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-201(2)(b): 26B-6-201 a vulnerable adult as defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-201(3): "Financial exploitation of an eligible adult" means:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-201(3)(a): the wrongful or unauthorized taking, withholding, appropriation, or use of money, assets, or other property of an eligible adult; or
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-201(3)(b): an act or omission, including through a power of attorney, guardianship, or conservatorship of an eligible adult, to:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-201(3)(b)(i): obtain control, through deception, intimidation, or undue influence, over an eligible adult's money, assets, or other property to deprive the eligible adult of the ownership, use, benefit, or possession of the eligible adult's money, assets, or other property; or
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-201(3)(b)(ii): convert an eligible adult's money, assets, or other property to deprive the eligible adult of the ownership, use, benefit, or possession of the eligible adult's money, assets, or other property.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-201(4): 53-1-102 "Law enforcement agency" means the same as that term is defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-201(5): "Qualified individual" means:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-201(5)(a): an agent;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-201(5)(b): an investment adviser representative; or
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-201(5)(c): an individual who serves in a supervisory, compliance, or legal capacity for a broker-dealer or an investment adviser.

Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-204 Delaying disbursements or transactions.
----------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-204(1): A broker-dealer or an investment adviser may delay a disbursement or transaction from an eligible adult's account or from an account on which the eligible adult is a beneficiary, if the broker-dealer or investment adviser:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-204(1)(a): suspects that the disbursement or transaction may result in the financial exploitation of an eligible adult;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-204(1)(b): initiates an internal review of the disbursement or transaction and the suspected financial exploitation of an eligible adult;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-204(1)(c): after initiating the internal review, reasonably believes that the disbursement or transaction may result in the financial exploitation of an eligible adult;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-204(1)(d): within two business days after the day on which the disbursement or transaction is delayed, provides written notification of the delay and the reason for the delay to:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-204(1)(d)(i): each party authorized to transact business on the account, unless the party is reasonably believed to have engaged in suspected or attempted financial exploitation of the eligible adult;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-204(1)(d)(ii): the division; and
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-204(1)(d)(iii): Adult Protective Services;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-204(1)(e): continues the broker-dealer's or investment adviser's internal review of the suspected or attempted financial exploitation of the eligible adult, as necessary; and
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-204(1)(f): upon request, provides a timely report on the status and results of the internal review to the division or Adult Protective Services.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-204(2): (3); (1) Except as provided in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-204(2)(a): the day on which the broker-dealer or investment adviser determines that the disbursement or transaction will not result in the financial exploitation of an eligible adult; or
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-204(2)(b): 15 business days after the day on which the broker-dealer or investment adviser initially delayed the disbursement or transaction.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-204(3): (1); (1) If an internal review described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-204(4): A court of competent jurisdiction may enter an order terminating or extending a delay under this section or granting other protective relief.

---------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 61-1-206(1): Upon request, a broker-dealer or investment adviser shall provide access to or a copy of any record, including a historical record, that is relevant to the suspected or attempted financial exploitation of an eligible adult to Adult Protective Services or a law enforcement agency.
