Utah Code Annotated § 61-2-201(1)(h): Chapter 2f, Real Estate Licensing and Practices Act
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2-201(1)(i): Chapter 2g, Real Estate Appraiser Licensing and Certification Act
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2-201(2): The division is under the direction and control of a director appointed by the executive director of the department with the approval of the governor.  The director holds the office of director at the pleasure of the governor.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2-201(3): The director, with the approval of the executive director, may employ personnel necessary to discharge the duties of the division at salaries to be fixed by the director according to standards established by the Division of Human Resource Management.


Utah Code Annotated § 61-2-202 Powers and duties of the director or division.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2-202(1): On or before October 1 of each year, in conjunction with the department, the director shall report to the governor and the Legislature concerning the division's work for the fiscal year immediately preceding the report.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2-202(2): In conjunction with the executive director, the director shall prepare and submit to the governor and the Legislature a budget for the fiscal year that follows the convening of the Legislature.

Utah Code Annotated § 61-2-203(7): Title 63G, Chapter 4, Administrative Procedures Act
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2-203(7)(a): Title 63G, Chapter 4, Administrative Procedures Act A citation issued by the division shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2-203(7)(a)(i): be in writing;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2-203(7)(a)(ii): describe with particularity the nature of the violation, including a reference to the provision of the statute, rule, or order alleged to have been violated;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2-203(7)(a)(iii): Title 63G, Chapter 4, Administrative Procedures Act clearly state that the recipient must notify the division in writing within 20 calendar days after the day on which the citation is served if the recipient wishes to contest the citation at a hearing conducted under
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2-203(7)(a)(iv): clearly explain the consequences of failure to timely contest the citation or to make payment of a fine assessed by the citation within the time period specified in the citation.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2-203(7)(b): The division may issue a notice in lieu of a citation.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2-203(8): 
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2-203(8)(a): A citation becomes final:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2-203(8)(a)(i): if within 20 calendar days after the day on which the citation is served, the person to whom the citation was issued fails to request a hearing to contest the citation; or
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2-203(8)(a)(ii): if the director or the director's designee conducts a hearing pursuant to a timely request for a hearing and issues an order finding that a violation has occurred.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2-203(8)(b): The division may extend, for cause, the 20-day period to contest a citation.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2-203(8)(c): A citation that becomes the final order of the division due to a person's failure to timely request a hearing is not subject to further agency review.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2-203(8)(d): 
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2-203(8)(d)(i): The division may refuse to issue, refuse to renew, suspend, revoke, or place on probation the license of a licensee who fails to comply with a citation after the citation becomes final.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2-203(8)(d)(ii): The failure of a license applicant to comply with a citation after the citation becomes final is a ground for denial of the license application.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2-203(9): 
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2-203(9)(a): The division may not issue a citation under this section after the expiration of one year after the day on which the violation occurs.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2-203(9)(b): The division may issue a notice to address a violation that is outside of the one-year citation period.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2-203(10): The director or the director's designee shall assess a fine with a citation in an amount that is no more than:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2-203(10)(a): for a first offense, $1,000;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2-203(10)(b): for a second offense, $2,000; and
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2-203(10)(c): for each offense subsequent to a second offense, $2,000 for each day of continued offense.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2-203(11): 
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2-203(11)(a): An action for a first or second offense for which the division has not issued a final order does not preclude the division from initiating a subsequent action for a second or subsequent offense while the preceding action is pending.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2-203(11)(b): The final order on a subsequent action is considered a second or subsequent offense, respectively, provided the preceding action resulted in a first or second offense, respectively.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2-203(12): 
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2-203(12)(a): If a person does not pay a penalty, the director may collect the unpaid penalty by:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2-203(12)(a)(i): referring the matter to a collection agency; or
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2-203(12)(a)(ii): bringing an action in the district court of the county:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2-203(12)(a)(ii)(A): where the person resides; or
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2-203(12)(a)(ii)(B): where the office of the director is located.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2-203(12)(b): A county attorney or the attorney general of the state shall provide legal services to the director in an action to collect the penalty.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2-203(12)(c): A court may award reasonable attorney fees and costs to the division in an action the division brings to enforce the provisions of this section.

Utah Code Annotated § 61-2-205 Concurrence.
-------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2-205(1): If a provision under this title requires concurrence between the director or division and a commission or board created under this title and no concurrence can be reached, the director or division has final authority.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2-205(2): (2) When this title requires concurrence between the director or division and a commission or board:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2-205(2)(a): the director or division shall report to and update the commission or board on a regular basis related to matters requiring concurrence; and
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2-205(2)(b): (2) the commission or board shall review the report submitted by the director or division under this Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2-205(2)(b)(i): provide a reason for not concurring with the report; and
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2-205(2)(b)(ii): provide recommendations to the director or division.


Utah Code Annotated - Title 61 - Chapter 2c - Utah Residential Mortgage Practices and Licensing Act
***************************************************************************************************

Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-101 Title.
--------------------------------------
This chapter is known as the "Utah Residential Mortgage Practices and Licensing Act."

Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-102 Definitions.
--------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-102(1): 61-2c-209; 61-2c-105; (1)(i)(ii); (1)(i)(i); 61-2c-204.1; 61-2c-104; 61-2c-204.1; 61-2c-205; 61-2c-105(2)(f); (1)(r)(i); (1)(r)(ii); 7-1-103; (1)(aa)(i); (1)(aa)(i); 61-2c-206; 61-2c-204.1; 61-2c-206; (1)(ff)(i); (1)(ff)(i); (1)(gg)(i); (1)(i)(ii)(A); Chapter 2f, Real Estate Licensing and Practices Act; 61-2c-204.1; 61-2c-206; 61-2c-206; (1)(oo)(i); 61-2c-209 As used in this chapter:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-102(1)(a): 61-2c-209 "Affiliation" means that a mortgage loan originator is associated with a principal lending manager in accordance with Section
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-102(1)(b): "Applicant" means a person applying for a license under this chapter.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-102(1)(c): "Approved examination provider" means a person approved by the nationwide database or by the division as an approved test provider.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-102(1)(d): "Associate lending manager" means an individual who:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-102(1)(d)(i): qualifies under this chapter as a principal lending manager; and
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-102(1)(d)(ii): works by or on behalf of another principal lending manager in transacting the business of residential mortgage loans.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-102(1)(e): "Balloon payment" means a required payment in a mortgage transaction that:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-102(1)(e)(i): results in a greater reduction in the principle of the mortgage than a regular installment payment; and
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-102(1)(e)(ii): is made during or at the end of the term of the loan.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-102(1)(f): "Branch lending manager" means an individual who is:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-102(1)(f)(i): licensed as a lending manager; and
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-102(1)(f)(ii): designated in the nationwide database by the individual's sponsoring entity as being responsible to work from a branch office and to supervise the business of residential mortgage loans that is conducted at the branch office.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-102(1)(g): "Branch office" means a licensed entity's office:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-102(1)(g)(i): for the transaction of the business of residential mortgage loans regulated under this chapter;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-102(1)(g)(ii): other than the main office of the licensed entity; and
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-102(1)(g)(iii): that operates under:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-102(1)(g)(iii)(A): the same business name as the licensed entity; or
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-102(1)(g)(iii)(B): another trade name that is registered with the division under the entity license.

Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-103 Powers and duties of the division.
------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-103(1): The division shall administer this chapter.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-103(2): (2)(c)(i); 63J-1-504 In addition to a power or duty expressly provided in this chapter, the division may:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-103(2)(a): receive and act on a complaint including:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-103(2)(a)(i): taking action designed to obtain voluntary compliance with this chapter; or
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-103(2)(a)(ii): commencing an administrative or judicial proceeding on the division's own initiative;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-103(2)(b): establish one or more programs for the education of consumers with respect to residential mortgage loans;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-103(2)(c): (2)(c)(i)
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-103(2)(c)(i): make one or more studies appropriate to effectuate the purposes and policies of this chapter; and
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-103(2)(c)(ii): (2)(c)(i) make the results of the studies described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-103(2)(d): visit and investigate a person licensed under this chapter, regardless of whether the person is located in Utah;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-103(2)(e): employ one or more necessary hearing examiners, investigators, clerks, and other employees and agents; and
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-103(2)(f): 63J-1-504 establish fees under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-103(2)(f)(i): processing an application for licensing or certification; and
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-103(2)(f)(ii): any other function required or permitted by this chapter.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-103(3): Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act The division shall make rules for the administration of this chapter in accordance with
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-103(3)(a): licensure procedures for:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-103(3)(a)(i): a person required by this chapter to obtain a license with the division; and
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-103(3)(a)(ii): the establishment of a branch office by an entity;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-103(3)(b): proper handling of money received by a licensee;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-103(3)(c): record-keeping requirements by a licensee, including proper disposal of a record;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-103(3)(d): certification procedures for certifying an education provider; and
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-103(3)(e): standards of conduct for a licensee or certified education provider.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-103(4): Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act The division may by rule made in accordance with
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-103(4)(a): required for uniformity amongst states; and
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-103(4)(b): not inconsistent with this chapter.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-103(5): Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act The division shall by rule made in accordance with
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-103(6): The division may enter into a relationship or contract with the nationwide database or another entity designated by the nationwide database to do the following related to a licensee or other person subject to this chapter:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-103(6)(a): collect or maintain a record; and
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-103(6)(b): process a transaction fee or other fee.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-103(7): The division shall regularly report the following to the nationwide database:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-103(7)(a): a violation of this chapter;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-103(7)(b): licensing or disciplinary action under this chapter; and
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-103(7)(c): other information relevant to this chapter.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-103(8): If a person pays a fee or costs to the division with a negotiable instrument or any other method that is not honored for payment:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-103(8)(a): the transaction for which the payment is submitted is voidable by the division;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-103(8)(b): the division may reverse the transaction if payment of the applicable fee or costs is not received in full; and
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-103(8)(c): the person's license, certification, or registration is automatically suspended:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-103(8)(c)(i): beginning the day on which the payment is due; and
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-103(8)(c)(ii): ending the day on which payment is made in full.


Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-104 Residential Mortgage Regulatory Commission.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-104(1): 
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-104(1)(a): There is created within the division the "Residential Mortgage Regulatory Commission" consisting of the following members appointed by the executive director with the approval of the governor:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-104(1)(a)(i): four members who:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-104(1)(a)(i)(A): have at least three years of experience in transacting the business of residential mortgage loans; and
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-104(1)(a)(i)(B): are licensed under this chapter at the time of and during appointment; and
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-104(1)(a)(ii): one member from the general public.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-104(1)(b): 
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-104(1)(b)(i): The executive director with the approval of the governor may appoint an alternate member to the board.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-104(1)(b)(ii): The alternate member shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-104(1)(b)(ii)(A): at the time of the appointment, have at least three years of experience in transacting the business of residential mortgage loans; and
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-104(1)(b)(ii)(B): be licensed under this chapter at the time of and during appointment.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-104(2): (2)(b); (2)(a)

Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-203 General qualifications for licensure.
---------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-203(1): Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act To qualify for licensure under this chapter, a person shall demonstrate through procedures established by rule made by the division in accordance with
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-203(1)(a): financial responsibility;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-203(1)(b): honesty, integrity, and truthfulness; and
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-203(1)(c): the competence to transact the business of residential mortgage loans, including general fitness such as to command the confidence of the community and to warrant a determination that the person will operate honestly, fairly, and efficiently within the purposes of this chapter.

Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-209 Sponsorship -- Affiliation.
-----------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-209(1): 
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-209(1)(a): The division may not license an individual, and an individual licensed under this chapter may not conduct the business of residential mortgage loans unless:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-209(1)(a)(i): if licensed as a mortgage loan originator, the individual:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-209(1)(a)(i)(A): is sponsored by an entity licensed under this chapter; and
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-209(1)(a)(i)(B): is affiliated with the sponsoring entity's principal lending manager; or
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-209(1)(a)(ii): if licensed as a lending manager, the individual is sponsored by an entity licensed under this chapter.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-209(1)(b): The division may not license an entity and an entity licensed under this chapter may not conduct the business of residential mortgage loans unless the entity:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-209(1)(b)(i): conducts the entity's business of residential mortgage loans from a location within the United States;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-209(1)(b)(ii): sponsors a principal lending manager;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-209(1)(b)(iii): identifies at least one control person for the entity; and
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-209(1)(b)(iv): provides a list of the mortgage loan originators sponsored by the entity.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-209(2): 
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-209(2)(a): A mortgage loan originator's license automatically becomes inactive the day on which:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-209(2)(a)(i): the mortgage loan originator is not sponsored by an entity licensed under this chapter;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-209(2)(a)(ii): the license of the entity with which the mortgage loan originator is sponsored becomes inactive or terminates;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-209(2)(a)(iii): the mortgage loan originator is not affiliated with a principal lending manager; or
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-209(2)(a)(iv): the license of the principal lending manager with whom the mortgage loan originator is affiliated becomes inactive or terminates.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-209(2)(b): A lending manager's license automatically becomes inactive the day on which:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-209(2)(b)(i): the lending manager is not sponsored by an entity licensed under this chapter; or
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-209(2)(b)(ii): the license of the entity with which the lending manager is sponsored becomes inactive or terminates.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-209(2)(c): An entity licensed under this chapter automatically becomes inactive the day on which the entity's sponsorship with the entity's principal lending manager terminates.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-209(3): 63J-1-504; 63J-1-504; 63J-1-504

Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-210 Surrender of license.
-----------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-210(1): The division may, by written agreement, accept the voluntary surrender of a license issued under this chapter.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-210(2): (1) Tender and acceptance of a voluntary surrender of a license under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-210(2)(a): does not prevent the division from pursuing additional action, including disciplinary action, that relates to the surrendered license and is authorized by this chapter or by rules made under this chapter; and
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-210(2)(b): terminates all rights and privileges associated with the license.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-210(3): (2)(b) A person may restore the rights and privileges described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-210(4): Any documentation relating to the tender and acceptance of a voluntary surrender is a public record.


Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-301 Prohibited conduct -- Violations of the chapter.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-301(1): (4); (5); 31A-2-402; 31A-2-405; 31A-2-405(2); 61-2c-105(4); Chapter 2, Division of Real Estate; Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act; Title 57, Chapter 28, Utah Reverse Mortgage Act A person transacting the business of residential mortgage loans in this state may not:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-301(1)(a): violate Section 8 of RESPA;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-301(1)(b): charge a fee in connection with a residential mortgage loan transaction:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-301(1)(b)(i): that is excessive; or
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-301(1)(b)(ii): without providing to the loan applicant a written statement signed by the loan applicant:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-301(1)(b)(ii)(A): stating whether or not the fee or deposit is refundable; and
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-301(1)(b)(ii)(B): describing the conditions, if any, under which all or a portion of the fee or deposit will be refunded to the loan applicant;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-301(1)(c): act incompetently in the transaction of the business of residential mortgage loans such that the person fails to:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-301(1)(c)(i): safeguard the interests of the public; or
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-301(1)(c)(ii): conform to acceptable standards of the residential mortgage loan industry;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-301(1)(d): do any of the following as part of a residential mortgage loan transaction, regardless of whether the residential mortgage loan closes:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-301(1)(d)(i): make a false statement or representation;

Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-403(1): Title 63G, Chapter 4, Administrative Procedures Act; (1)(b)
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-403(1)(a): The director may issue and serve by certified mail, or by personal service, on a person an order to cease and desist from an act if:

----------------------------------------------

Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-404(1)(a)(i): commission;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-404(1)(a)(ii): compensation; or
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-404(1)(a)(iii): profit.

Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-404(2): A person who is not licensed under this chapter at the time of an act or service that requires a license under this chapter may not bring an action in court for the recovery of a commission, fee, or compensation for that act or service.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-404(3): 
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-404(3)(a): A mortgage loan originator may not bring an action in the mortgage loan originator's own name for the recovery of a fee, commission, or compensation for transacting the business of residential mortgage loans unless the action is brought against the entity by which the mortgage loan originator is sponsored at the time of the act or service that is the subject of the action.

Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-404(3)(b)(i): an entity; or
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-404(3)(b)(ii): the principal lending manager of an entity on behalf of the entity.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-404(4): A principal lending manager who transacts the business of residential mortgage loans on the principal lending manager's own behalf may sue in the principal lending manager's own name for the recovery of a fee, commission, or compensation for transacting the business of residential mortgage loans.


Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-405 Penalty for violating this chapter -- Automatic revocation.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-405(1): In addition to being subject to a disciplinary action by the commission, a person required to be licensed or certified under this chapter who violates this chapter:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-405(1)(a): is guilty of a class A misdemeanor upon conviction of a first violation of this chapter; and
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-405(1)(b): is guilty of a third degree felony upon conviction of a second or subsequent violation of this chapter.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-405(2): 76-6-1203 A license or certification issued by the division to a person convicted of a violation of Section


Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-501 Fund created.
---------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-501(1): There is created an expendable special revenue fund known as the "Residential Mortgage Loan Education, Research, and Recovery Fund."
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-501(2): The interest earned on the fund shall be deposited into the fund.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-501(3): At the beginning of each fiscal year, the division shall make available


Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-501.5 Definitions.
----------------------------------------------
As used in this part:Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-501.5(1): "Civil judgment" means a judgment in a civil action that:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-501.5(1)(a): is awarded in an action brought against a person licensed under this chapter on the basis of fraud, misrepresentation, or deceit in a residential mortgage loan transaction; and
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-501.5(1)(b): awards actual damages.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-501.5(2): "Criminal restitution judgment" means a judgment that, in accordance with the Utah Code of Criminal Procedure, orders criminal restitution to a person and against a person licensed under this chapter for a criminal offense involving fraud, misrepresentation, or deceit in a residential mortgage loan transaction.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-501.5(3): "Final judgment" means one of the following judgments upon termination of the proceedings related to the judgment, including appeals:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-501.5(3)(a): a civil judgment; or
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-501.5(3)(b): a criminal restitution judgment.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-501.5(4): 61-2c-501 "Fund" means the Residential Mortgage Loan Education, Research, and Recovery Fund created in Section

Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-503 Notice to division -- Judgment against mortgage licensee -- Fraud, misrepresentation, or deceit -- Verified petition for order directing payment from fund -- Limitations and procedure.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-503(1): A person may bring a claim against the fund if:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-503(1)(a): the person obtains a final judgment;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-503(1)(b): the person complies with the requirements under this part;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-503(1)(c): the person is not complicit in the fraud, misrepresentation, or deceit that is the basis of the claim; and
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-503(1)(d): the final judgment that is the basis for the claim:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-503(1)(d)(i): has not been discharged in bankruptcy; and
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-503(1)(d)(ii): when a bankruptcy proceeding is open or commenced during the pendency of the claim, the person obtains an order from the bankruptcy court declaring the final judgment and related debt to be nondischargeable.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-503(2): (1)

Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-503(2)(b): (1) Within 30 calendar days of the day on which the division receives a notice under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-503(3): (3)(a)(i)

Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-505 Court determination and order.
--------------------------------------------------------------
If the court determines that a claim should be levied against the portion of the fund allocated to carry out this chapter, the court shall enter an order requiring the division to pay from the fund the portion of a final judgment that is payable from the fund under Section

Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-506 Insufficient funds to satisfy judgment -- Procedure and interest.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
If the money deposited in the fund and allotted for satisfying judgments against licensees is insufficient to satisfy an authorized claim for payment, the division shall, when sufficient money has been deposited in the fund, satisfy the unpaid claims in the order they originally were filed, together with accumulated interest at the rate allowable on judgments under Section

Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-507(2)(b)(i)(B): Title 63G, Chapter 4, Administrative Procedures Act in accordance with
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-507(2)(b)(ii): (2)(b)(i) The commission may delegate:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-507(2)(b)(ii)(A): (2)(b)(i) to the division or an administrative law judge the authority to conduct a hearing described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-507(2)(b)(ii)(B): to the division the authority to make a decision on whether relief from a suspension should be granted.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-507(3): (2)(b); (2) Unless the suspension is not upheld after a hearing described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-507(3)(a): pays into the fund:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-507(3)(a)(i): the amount paid out of the fund on behalf of the licensee; and
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-507(3)(a)(ii): interest at a rate determined by the division with the concurrence of the commission; and
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-507(3)(b): participates in a hearing before the commission and is approved by the commission, with the concurrence of the director, for licensure or activation of the suspended license.


Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-508 Failure to comply.
--------------------------------------------------
The failure of a person to comply with this part is a waiver of any right provided under this part.

Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-509 Disciplinary actions.
-----------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-509(1): This part does not limit the authority of the director or commission to take disciplinary action against a licensee for a violation of:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-509(1)(a): this chapter; or
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-509(1)(b): rules made by the division under this chapter.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-509(2): The repayment in full of all obligations to the fund by a licensee does not nullify or modify the effect of a disciplinary proceeding brought under:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-509(2)(a): this chapter; or
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-509(2)(b): rules made by the division under this chapter.


Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-510 Money accumulated -- Purpose.
-------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-510(1): The division may use money accumulated in the fund in excess of the amount necessary to satisfy claims to:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-510(1)(a): investigate violations of this chapter related to fraud; and
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-510(1)(b): advance education and research in the field of residential mortgage loans.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-510(2): (1); (1) The division may use the excess money described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-510(2)(a): courses sponsored by the division;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-510(2)(b): courses offered by the division in conjunction with a university or college in Utah;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-510(2)(c): contracting for a research project for the state in the field of residential mortgage loans;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-510(2)(d): funding the salaries and training expenses of division staff members who are employed in positions related to the education of mortgage licensees;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-510(2)(e): funding the training expenses of division staff members who are employed in positions conducting investigations of complaints under this chapter; and
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-510(2)(f): publishing and distributing educational materials to:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-510(2)(f)(i): licensees; and
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2c-510(2)(f)(ii): applicants for licensure.


Utah Code Annotated - Title 61 - Chapter 2d - Utah High Cost Home Loan Act
**************************************************************************

Utah Code Annotated § 61-2d-101 Title.
--------------------------------------
This chapter is known as the "Utah High Cost Home Loan Act."

Utah Code Annotated § 61-2d-102 Definitions.
--------------------------------------------
As used in this part:Utah Code Annotated § 61-2d-102(1): "Accelerate" means a demand for immediate repayment of the entire balance of a residential mortgage loan.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2d-102(2): "Borrower" means a person that:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2d-102(2)(a): seeks a high-cost mortgage; or
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2d-102(2)(b): is obligated under a high-cost mortgage.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2d-102(3): Title 61, Chapter 2c, Utah Residential Mortgage Practices and Licensing Act "High-cost mortgage" means a borrower credit transaction that is secured by the borrower's principal dwelling, if any of the following apply with respect to such borrower credit transaction:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2d-102(3)(a): the transaction is secured by a first mortgage on the borrower's principal dwelling and the annual percentage rate on the credit, at the consummation of the transaction, will exceed by more than eight percentage points the yield on treasury securities having comparable periods of maturity on the 15th day of the month immediately preceding the month in which the application for the extension of credit is received by the lender;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2d-102(3)(b): the transaction is secured by a junior or subordinate mortgage on the borrower's principal dwelling and the annual percentage rate on the credit, at the consummation of the transaction, will exceed 10 percentage points the yield on treasury securities having comparable periods of maturity on the 15th day of the month immediately preceding the month in which the application for the extension of credit is received by the lender; or
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2d-102(3)(c): 
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2d-102(3)(c)(i): the total points and fees payable at or before the transaction will exceed the greater of 8% of the total loan amount or $400;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2d-102(3)(c)(ii): 
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2d-102(3)(c)(ii)(A): the $400 figure shall be adjusted annually on January 1 to match the adjusted number adopted by the Board of Governors of the Federal Reserve in accordance with Section 226.32(a)(1)(ii) of the Code of Federal Regulations; or
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2d-102(3)(c)(ii)(B): if the Board of Governors of the Federal Reserve System does not announce an adjusted figure, the last adjustment of the $400 figure shall be adjusted annually on January 1 by the annual percentage change in the Consumer Price Index that was reported on the preceding June 1; and
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2d-102(3)(d): Title 61, Chapter 2c, Utah Residential Mortgage Practices and Licensing Act the loan is made by or originated through a person or business required to hold a license as provided in
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2d-102(4): Title 61, Chapter 2c, Utah Residential Mortgage Practices and Licensing Act "Lender" means a person that:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2d-102(4)(a): offers a high-cost mortgage; or
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2d-102(4)(b): extends a high-cost mortgage; and
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2d-102(4)(c): Title 61, Chapter 2c, Utah Residential Mortgage Practices and Licensing Act is required to have a license as provided in
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2d-102(5): "Prepay" or "prepayment" means to make a payment to a lender that:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2d-102(5)(a): is more than the amount of the next scheduled payment due;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2d-102(5)(b): pays more than half of the principal balance of the high-cost mortgage; and
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2d-102(5)(c): is paid more than 24 months before the last scheduled payment according to the terms of the high-cost mortgage when it is made.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2d-102(6): "Residential mortgage transaction" means a transaction in which a mortgage, deed of trust, purchase money security interest arising under an installment sales contract, or equivalent consensual security interest is created or retained in the borrower's principal dwelling to finance the acquisition or initial construction of that dwelling.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2d-102(7): "Reverse mortgage transaction" means a nonrecourse borrower credit obligation in which:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2d-102(7)(a): a mortgage, deed of trust, or equivalent consensual security interest securing one or more advances is created in the borrower's principal dwelling; and
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2d-102(7)(b): any principal, interest, or shared appreciation or equity is due and payable, other than in the case of default, only after:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2d-102(7)(b)(i): the borrower dies;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2d-102(7)(b)(ii): the dwelling is transferred; or
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2d-102(7)(b)(iii): the borrower ceases to occupy the dwelling as a principal dwelling.


Utah Code Annotated § 61-2d-103 Prepayment penalty.
---------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2d-103(1): The terms of a high-cost mortgage loan may contain terms under which a borrower must pay a penalty for prepayment.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2d-103(1)(a): However, a penalty for prepayment cannot be assessed more than 36 months after the loan was originally made.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2d-103(1)(b): The amount of the penalty may not exceed the total amount of interest paid at 80% of the immediately preceding six scheduled payments.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2d-103(2): For purposes of this section, any method of computing a refund or unearned scheduled interest is a prepayment penalty if it is less favorable to the borrower than the actuarial method.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2d-103(3): (1) Notwithstanding Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2d-103(3)(a): the high-cost mortgage is paid with the proceeds of a new loan by the same lender or an affiliate of that lender; or
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2d-103(3)(b): the penalty is prohibited under other applicable law.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2d-103(4): If a prepayment does not pay the full amount owed on the high-cost mortgage when the prepayment is made, the penalty shall be reduced by a percentage equal to the percentage of the balance owed before the prepayment that remains unpaid.


Utah Code Annotated § 61-2d-104 Negative amortization prohibited.
-----------------------------------------------------------------
A high cost mortgage shall provide for regular, periodic payments sufficient to pay:Utah Code Annotated § 61-2d-104(1): all accrued interest and a portion of principal on the scheduled due date for each payment; and
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2d-104(2): the full amount owed during the term of the loan, if no late fees or other contingent charges are incurred.


Utah Code Annotated § 61-2d-105 Financing points and fees -- Restrictions.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2d-105(1): A lender may not, in connection with the formation or consummation of a high-cost mortgage, finance, directly or indirectly, any portion of the points, fees, or other charges payable to the lender or any third party in an amount in excess of 8% of the total loan amount, unless the following additional disclosures are made to the borrower in conspicuous type size:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2d-105(1)(a): "You are not required to complete this agreement merely because you have received these disclosures or have signed the loan application."
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2d-105(1)(b): "If you obtain this loan, the lender will have a mortgage on your home.  You could lose your home or property, and any money you have put into it, if you do not meet your obligations under this loan."
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2d-105(1)(c): "The timing and amount of payments on debts you already are carrying contribute to the credit rating that is used to determine whether you may get a new loan and how much you will pay for that new loan.  You should not accept any advice to ignore or delay making any payment on loans you already have, even if those loans will be paid off with the new loan."
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2d-105(1)(d): "You may get into serious financial difficulties if you use this loan to pay off old debts and then run up other new debts."
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2d-105(2): The disclosures required by this section shall be given to the borrower no less than three business days prior to consummation of the transaction.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2d-105(3): After providing the disclosure required by this section, a lender may not change the terms of the extension of credit if such changes make the disclosures inaccurate, unless new disclosures are provided that meet the requirements of this section.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2d-105(4): (3) A lender may provide new disclosures pursuant to Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2d-105(4)(a): the change is initiated by the borrower; and
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2d-105(4)(b): at the consummation of the transaction under which the credit is extended:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2d-105(4)(b)(i): the lender provides to the borrower the new disclosures in writing; and
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2d-105(4)(b)(ii): the lender and borrower certify in writing that the new disclosures were provided by telephone, at least three days prior to the date of consummation of the transaction.


Utah Code Annotated § 61-2d-106 Arbitration clauses.
----------------------------------------------------
To be valid, an arbitration clause in a high-cost mortgage contract must comply with the standards set forth in

Utah Code Annotated § 61-2d-107 Prohibition on single premium credit life insurance.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
A borrower credit transaction involving a high-cost mortgage may not include:Utah Code Annotated § 61-2d-107(1): the offer or sale of any insurance policy, on a single premium or single fee basis, that insures, guarantees, or indemnifies the repayment of the outstanding balance of the loan against:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2d-107(1)(a): death;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2d-107(1)(b): illness;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2d-107(1)(c): accident;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2d-107(1)(d): disability; or
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2d-107(1)(e): unemployment of the borrower; or
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2d-107(2): debt cancellation or a debt suspension agreement.


Utah Code Annotated § 61-2d-108 Increase in employees.
------------------------------------------------------
Funds allocated for investigations in this chapter may only be used to employ additional employees if there is a 10% increase in caseloads.

Utah Code Annotated § 61-2d-109 Copies.
---------------------------------------
The lender shall provide, at no cost to the borrower, a complete set of all documents pertaining to the transaction, including copies of all documents to be executed or recorded and any loan documents changed at the closing:Utah Code Annotated § 61-2d-109(1): at the time of the closing if done in person; or
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2d-109(2): no later than three business days from the closing if done by mail or any other format.


Utah Code Annotated § 61-2d-110 Encouraging default prohibited.
---------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2d-110(1): A lender may not recommend or encourage default or nonpayment leading to foreclosure on an existing loan or other debt prior to and in connection with the closing or planned closing of a high-cost mortgage that refinances all or any portion of such existing loan or debt.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2d-110(2): This section applies to all loans.


Utah Code Annotated § 61-2d-111 Mortgage forms.
-----------------------------------------------
All lines, figures, forms, and blanks that regulate, govern, control, and authorize a mortgage must be filled in before the documents are signed.

Utah Code Annotated § 61-2d-112 Notice of information available to borrowers.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2d-112(1): In addition to any other notice or disclosure a lender or title company may provide to a borrower seeking, obtaining, or inquiring about a high-cost mortgage, the lender shall provide the borrower any brochure or other document information prepared by a federal or state authority in a form intended to inform consumers about home loans or consumer credit on financing or educational resources on financing.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2d-112(2): (1) The requirement set forth in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2d-112(2)(a): the posting, in a public area of the office, notice indicating that educational resources are available;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2d-112(2)(b): a list of educational opportunities or programs offered in the surrounding area including the program name and phone number;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2d-112(2)(c): a printed brochure or booklet on responsible lending and borrowing available to the borrower at no charge; or
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2d-112(2)(d): information from the Department of Financial Institutions on its responsible consumer financial educational program.


Utah Code Annotated § 61-2d-113 Effect of failure to comply.
------------------------------------------------------------
Failure to provide the notices or information described in Subsection

Utah Code Annotated § 61-2e-101 Title.

Utah Code Annotated § 61-2e-102(5)(c)(iii): collecting a fee from a client for a service provided; or
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2e-102(5)(c)(iv): paying an appraiser for a real estate appraisal activity; or
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2e-102(5)(d): reviewing or verifying the work of an appraiser.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2e-102(6): 61-2g-102 "Appraisal report" means the same as that term is defined in Section

Utah Code Annotated § 61-2e-102(9):

Utah Code Annotated § 61-2e-102(9)(a)(ii): approved by an appraisal management company to perform appraisals as independent contractors for the appraisal management company.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2e-102(9)(b): "Appraiser panel" includes an appraiser whom the appraisal management company has:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2e-102(9)(b)(i): accepted for consideration for a future appraisal assignment:

Utah Code Annotated § 61-2e-102(9)(b)(ii)(B): for a secondary mortgage market participant in connection with a residential mortgage loan transaction.

Utah Code Annotated § 61-2e-102(16): 61-2-201 "Division" means the Division of Real Estate, created in Section

Utah Code Annotated § 61-2e-104 Exemption.
------------------------------------------
This chapter does not apply to:Utah Code Annotated § 61-2e-104(1): an entity that:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2e-104(1)(a): exclusively employs an individual on an employer-employee basis for the performance of a real estate appraisal activity in the normal course of the entity's business;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2e-104(1)(b): is responsible for ensuring that the real estate appraisal activity being performed by an employee is performed in accordance with applicable appraisal standards; and
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2e-104(1)(c): is a federally regulated appraisal management company;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2e-104(2): an individual who:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2e-104(2)(a): is an appraiser; and
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2e-104(2)(b): in the normal course of business enters into an agreement, whether written or otherwise, with another appraiser for the performance of a real estate appraisal activity that the individual cannot complete for any reason, including:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2e-104(2)(b)(i): competency;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2e-104(2)(b)(ii): work load;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2e-104(2)(b)(iii): schedule; or
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2e-104(2)(b)(iv): geographic location; or
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2e-104(3): an individual who:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2e-104(3)(a): in the normal course of business enters into an agreement, whether written or otherwise, with an appraiser for the performance of a real estate appraisal activity; and
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2e-104(3)(b): under the agreement, cosigns the report of the appraiser performing the real estate appraisal activity upon the completion of the real estate appraisal activity.

Utah Code Annotated § 61-2e-201(4)(d)(iii): has not had a license or certificate to engage in an act related to a real estate or mortgage transaction refused, denied, canceled, or revoked in any state, territory, or the District of Columbia.

Utah Code Annotated § 61-2e-204(4)(a): 
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2e-204(4)(a)(i): a conviction of a criminal offense;

Utah Code Annotated § 61-2e-204(5): A registration expires if it is not renewed on or before its expiration date, except that for a period of one year after the expiration date, the registration may be reinstated upon compliance with this section, including payment of a renewal fee and a late fee determined by the division and the board.

Utah Code Annotated § 61-2e-302 Adherence to standards.
-------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2e-302(1): An appraisal management company required to be registered under this chapter shall have a system in place to:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2e-302(1)(a): ensure that the appraisal management company only selects for a real estate appraisal activity an appraiser who:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2e-302(1)(a)(i): is independent of the transaction; and
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2e-302(1)(a)(ii): has the requisite education, expertise, and experience necessary to competently complete the real estate appraisal activity for the particular market and property type;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2e-302(1)(b): review the work of an appraiser who performs a real estate appraisal activity for the appraisal management company on a periodic basis to ensure that a real estate appraisal activity is conducted in accordance with applicable appraisal standards; and
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2e-302(1)(c): ensure that the appraisal management company conducts appraisal management services in accordance with the requirements of the Truth in Lending Act, 15 U.S.C. Sec. 1639e(a)-(i), and the regulations thereunder.

Utah Code Annotated § 61-2e-304 Required disclosure -- Customary and reasonable compensation.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2e-304(1): Before an appraisal management company may receive money from a client for a real estate appraisal activity requested by the client, the appraisal management company shall disclose to the client the total compensation that the appraisal management company pays to the appraiser who performs the real estate appraisal activity.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2e-304(2): An appraisal management company shall compensate an appraiser for an appraisal at a rate that is:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2e-304(2)(a): customary and reasonable for an appraisal in the geographic market area of the property being appraised; and
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2e-304(2)(b): consistent with a presumption of compliance under the Dodd-Frank Wall Street Reform and Consumer Protection Act, Pub. L. No. 111-203, and implementing federal regulations.

Utah Code Annotated § 61-2e-307 Prohibited acts -- Exclusions.
--------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2e-307(1): An appraisal management company required to be registered under this chapter and a controlling person, employee, or agent of the appraisal management company may not:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2e-307(1)(a): engage in an act of coercion, extortion, intimidation, or bribery for any purpose related to an appraisal;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2e-307(1)(b): compensate an appraiser in a manner that the person should reasonably know would result in the appraiser not conducting a real estate appraisal activity in a manner consistent with applicable appraisal standards;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2e-307(1)(c): engage in the business of an appraisal management company under an assumed or fictitious name not properly registered in the state;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2e-307(1)(d): accept a contingent fee for performing an appraisal management service if the fee is contingent on:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2e-307(1)(d)(i): the appraisal report having a predetermined analysis, opinion, or conclusion;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2e-307(1)(d)(ii): the analysis, opinion, conclusion, or valuation reached in an appraisal report; or
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2e-307(1)(d)(iii): the consequences resulting from the appraisal assignment;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2e-307(1)(e): require an appraiser to indemnify the appraisal management company against liability except liability for errors and omissions by the appraiser;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2e-307(1)(f): alter, modify, or otherwise change a completed appraisal report submitted by an appraiser; or
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2e-307(1)(g): engage in any act or practice that violates appraisal independence as defined in 15 U.S.C. Sec. 1639e or in the policies and procedures of:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2e-307(1)(g)(i): the Federal Home Loan Mortgage Corporation; or
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2e-307(1)(g)(ii): the Federal National Mortgage Association.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2e-307(2): An appraisal management company required to be registered under this chapter, or a controlling person, employee, or agent of the appraisal management company may not influence or attempt to influence the development, reporting, or review of an appraisal through:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2e-307(2)(a): coercion;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2e-307(2)(b): extortion;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2e-307(2)(c): collusion;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2e-307(2)(d): compensation;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2e-307(2)(e): instruction;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2e-307(2)(f): inducement;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2e-307(2)(g): intimidation;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2e-307(2)(h): bribery; or
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2e-307(2)(i): any other manner that would constitute undue influence.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2e-307(3): (2); (2); 61-2e-306 A violation of Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2e-307(3)(a): withholding or threatening to withhold timely payment for an appraisal;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2e-307(3)(b): withholding or threatening to withhold future business for an appraiser;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2e-307(3)(c): taking adverse action or threatening to take adverse action against an appraiser regarding use of the appraiser for a real estate appraisal activity;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2e-307(3)(d): expressly or by implication promising future business or increased compensation for an appraiser;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2e-307(3)(e): conditioning one or more of the following on the opinion, conclusion, or valuation to be reached, or on a preliminary estimate or opinion requested from an appraiser:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2e-307(3)(e)(i): a request for a real estate appraisal activity; or
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2e-307(3)(e)(ii): the payment of consideration;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2e-307(3)(f): requesting that an appraiser provide at any time before the appraiser's completion of a real estate appraisal activity:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2e-307(3)(f)(i): an estimated, predetermined, or desired valuation in an appraisal report; or
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2e-307(3)(f)(ii): an estimated value or comparable sale;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2e-307(3)(g): except for a copy of a sales contract for a purchase transaction, providing to an appraiser:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2e-307(3)(g)(i): an anticipated, estimated, encouraged, or desired value for a subject property; or
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2e-307(3)(g)(ii): a proposed or target amount to be loaned to the borrower;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2e-307(3)(h): providing to an appraiser, or an individual related to the appraiser, stock or other financial or non-financial benefits;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2e-307(3)(i): 61-2e-306 allowing the removal of an appraiser from an appraiser panel, without prior written notice to the appraiser as required by Section
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2e-307(3)(j): obtaining, using, or paying for a subsequent appraisal or ordering an automated valuation model in connection with a mortgage financing transaction unless:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2e-307(3)(j)(i): 
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2e-307(3)(j)(i)(A): there is a reasonable basis to believe that the initial appraisal does not meet applicable appraisal standards; and
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2e-307(3)(j)(i)(B): the reasonable basis is noted in the loan file; or
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2e-307(3)(j)(ii): the subsequent appraisal or automated valuation model is done pursuant to a pre- or post-funding appraisal review or quality control process in accordance with applicable appraisal standards;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2e-307(3)(k): removing or threatening to remove an appraiser from the appraiser panel if an appraiser requires a reasonable extension of the completion date for an appraisal assignment in order to complete a credible appraisal report; or
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2e-307(3)(l): engaging in any other act or practice that impairs or attempts to impair an appraiser's independence, objectivity, or impartiality.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2e-307(4): This section may not be construed to prohibit an appraisal management company from requesting that an appraiser:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2e-307(4)(a): provide additional information about the basis for a valuation; or
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2e-307(4)(b): correct an objective factual error in an appraisal report.


Utah Code Annotated § 61-2e-401 Division authority -- Immunity -- Transmission of reports to Appraisal Subcommittee.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2e-401(1): 
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2e-401(1)(a): In addition to a power or duty expressly provided in this chapter, the division may:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2e-401(1)(a)(i): examine any book or record of an appraisal management company registered or required to be registered under this chapter and require the appraisal management company to submit any report, information, or document to the division;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2e-401(1)(a)(ii): receive and act on a complaint including:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2e-401(1)(a)(ii)(A): taking action designed to obtain voluntary compliance with this chapter, including the issuance of a cease and desist order if the person against whom the order is issued is given the right to petition the board for review of the order; or
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2e-401(1)(a)(ii)(B): commencing an administrative or judicial proceeding on the division's own initiative;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2e-401(1)(a)(iii): conduct a public or private investigation of an entity required to be registered under this chapter, regardless of whether the entity is located in Utah;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2e-401(1)(a)(iv): employ one or more investigators, clerks, or other employees or agents if:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2e-401(1)(a)(iv)(A): approved by the executive director; and
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2e-401(1)(a)(iv)(B): within the budget of the division; and
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2e-401(1)(a)(v): issue a subpoena that requires:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2e-401(1)(a)(v)(A): the attendance and testimony of a witness; or
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2e-401(1)(a)(v)(B): the production of evidence.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2e-401(1)(b): 
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2e-401(1)(b)(i): A court of competent jurisdiction shall enforce, according to the practice and procedure of the court, a subpoena issued by the division.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2e-401(1)(b)(ii): The division shall pay any witness fee, travel expense, mileage, or any other fee required by the service statutes of the state where the witness or evidence is located.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2e-401(1)(c): A failure to respond to a request by the division in an investigation under this chapter within 10 days after the day on which the request is served is considered to be a separate violation of this chapter, including:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2e-401(1)(c)(i): failing to respond to a subpoena;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2e-401(1)(c)(ii): withholding evidence; or
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2e-401(1)(c)(iii): failing to produce a document or record.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2e-401(2): The division is immune from a civil action or criminal prosecution for initiating or assisting in a lawful investigation of an act or participating in a disciplinary proceeding under this chapter if the division takes the action:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2e-401(2)(a): without malicious intent; and
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2e-401(2)(b): in the reasonable belief that the action is taken pursuant to the powers and duties vested in the division under this chapter.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2e-401(3): Upon the Appraisal Subcommittee's request, the division shall timely transmit a report to the Appraisal Subcommittee regarding the division's supervisory activities involving appraisal management companies or other third-party providers of appraisals and appraisal management services, including any investigation the division initiates or disciplinary action the division takes.

Utah Code Annotated - Title 61 - Chapter 2f - Real Estate Licensing and Practices Act
*************************************************************************************

Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-101 Title.
--------------------------------------
This chapter is known as the "Real Estate Licensing and Practices Act."

Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-102 Definitions.
--------------------------------------------
As used in this chapter:Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-102(1): (20) "Associate broker" means an individual who is:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-102(1)(a): (20) employed or engaged as an independent contractor by or on behalf of a principal broker to perform an act described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-102(1)(b): licensed under this chapter as an associate broker.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-102(2): "Branch broker" means an associate broker who manages a principal broker's branch office under the supervision of the principal broker.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-102(3): "Branch office" means a principal broker's real estate brokerage office that is not the principal broker's main office.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-102(4): "Business day" means a day other than:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-102(4)(a): a Saturday;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-102(4)(b): a Sunday; or
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-102(4)(c): a federal or state holiday.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-102(5): "Business opportunity" means the sale, lease, or exchange of any business that includes an interest in real estate.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-102(6): "Commission" means the Real Estate Commission established under this chapter.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-102(7): "Concurrence" means the entities given a concurring role must jointly agree for action to be taken.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-102(8): "Condominium homeowners' association" means the condominium unit owners acting as a group in accordance with declarations and bylaws.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-102(9): 
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-102(9)(a): "Condominium hotel" means one or more condominium units that are operated as a hotel.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-102(9)(b): "Condominium hotel" does not mean a hotel consisting of condominium units, all of which are owned by a single entity.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-102(10): 57-8-3 "Condominium unit" means the same as that term is defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-102(11): "Director" means the director of the Division of Real Estate.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-102(12): "Division" means the Division of Real Estate.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-102(13): "Dual broker" means a principal broker of a real estate sales brokerage who obtains from the division a dual broker license in order to function as the principal broker of a property management company that is a separate entity from the real estate sales brokerage.

Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-102(21): 
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-102(21)(a): "Property management" means engaging in, with the expectation of receiving valuable consideration, the management of real estate owned by another person or advertising or otherwise claiming to be engaged in property management by:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-102(21)(a)(i): advertising for, arranging, negotiating, offering, or otherwise attempting or participating in a transaction calculated to secure the rental or leasing of real estate;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-102(21)(a)(ii): collecting, agreeing, offering, or otherwise attempting to collect rent for the real estate and accounting for and disbursing the money collected; or
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-102(21)(a)(iii): authorizing expenditures for repairs to the real estate.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-102(21)(b): "Property management" does not include:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-102(21)(b)(i): hotel or motel management;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-102(21)(b)(ii): rental of tourist accommodations, including hotels, motels, tourist homes, condominiums, condominium hotels, mobile home park accommodations, campgrounds, or similar public accommodations for a period of less than 30 consecutive days, and the management activities associated with these rentals; or
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-102(21)(b)(iii): the leasing or management of surface or subsurface minerals or oil and gas interests, if the leasing or management is separate from a sale or lease of the surface estate.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-102(22): "Property management sales agent" means a sales agent who:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-102(22)(a): is affiliated with a dual broker through the dual broker's property management company; and
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-102(22)(b): is designated by the dual broker as a property management sales agent.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-102(23): "Real estate" includes leaseholds and business opportunities involving real property.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-102(24): 
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-102(24)(a): "Regular salaried employee" means an individual who performs a service for wages or other remuneration, whose employer withholds federal employment taxes under a contract of hire, written or oral, express or implied.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-102(24)(b): "Regular salaried employee" does not include an individual who performs services on a project-by-project basis or on a commission basis.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-102(25): "Reinstatement" means restoring a license that has expired or has been suspended.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-102(26): "Reissuance" means the process by which a licensee may obtain a license following revocation of the license.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-102(27): "Renewal" means extending a license for an additional licensing period on or before the date the license expires.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-102(28): 61-2f-303; (20) "Sales agent" means an individual who is:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-102(28)(a): 61-2f-303; (20) affiliated with a principal broker, either as an independent contractor or an employee as provided in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-102(28)(b): licensed under this chapter as a sales agent.

Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-106 Severability.
---------------------------------------------
If a provision of this chapter, or the application of a provision to any person or circumstance, is held invalid, the remainder of this chapter shall be given effect without the invalid provision or application.  The provisions of this chapter are severable.

Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-201 License required.
-------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-201(1): Unless a person is licensed under this chapter, it is unlawful for the person to do the following with respect to real estate located in this state:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-201(1)(a): engage in the business of a principal broker, associate broker, or sales agent;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-201(1)(b): act in the capacity of a principal broker, associate broker, or sales agent;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-201(1)(c): advertise or assume to act as a principal broker, associate broker, or a sales agent.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-201(2): 61-2f-202 Except as provided in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-201(2)(a): buying, selling, leasing, managing, or exchanging real estate for another person; or
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-201(2)(b): offering for another person to buy, sell, lease, manage, or exchange real estate.

Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-207 Change of information -- Failure to notify.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-207(1): An applicant, licensee, registrant, or certificate holder shall send the division a signed statement in the form required by the division notifying the division within 10 business days of any change of:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-207(1)(a): principal broker;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-207(1)(b): principal business location;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-207(1)(c): mailing address;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-207(1)(d): home street address;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-207(1)(e): an individual's name; or
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-207(1)(f): business name.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-207(2): 
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-207(2)(a): When providing the division a business location or home street address, a physical location or street address must be provided.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-207(2)(b): When providing a mailing address, an applicant, licensee, registrant, or certificate holder may provide a post office box or other mail drop location.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-207(3): (1) Failure to notify the division of a change described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-207(4): An applicant, licensee, registrant, or certificate holder is considered to have received any notification that has been sent to the last address furnished to the division by the applicant, licensee, registrant, or certificate holder.


Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-208 Surrender of license.
-----------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-208(1): The division may, by written agreement, accept the voluntary surrender of a license issued under this chapter.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-208(2): (1) Tender and acceptance of a voluntary surrender of a license under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-208(2)(a): does not prevent the division from pursuing additional action, including disciplinary action, that relates to the surrendered license and is authorized by this chapter or by rules made under this chapter; and
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-208(2)(b): terminates all rights and privileges associated with the license.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-208(3): (2)(b) A person may restore the rights and privileges described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-208(4): Any documentation relating to the tender and acceptance of a voluntary surrender is a public record.

Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-302 Affiliation with a principal broker.
--------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-302(1): 61-2f-201 An individual who is not a principal broker may not engage in an act described in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-302(1)(a): an associate broker; or
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-302(1)(b): a sales agent.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-302(2): 
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-302(2)(a): An inactive associate broker or sales agent may not conduct a real estate transaction until the inactive associate broker or sales agent becomes affiliated with a principal broker and submits the required documentation to the division.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-302(2)(b): An inactive principal broker may not conduct a real estate transaction until the principal broker's license is activated with the division.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-302(3): A sales agent or associate broker may not affiliate with more than one principal broker at the same time.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-302(4): An individual may not be a principal broker of an entity and a sales agent or associate broker for a different entity at the same time.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-302(5): An owner, purchaser, lessor, or lessee who engages the services of a principal broker may designate which sales agents or associate brokers affiliated with that principal broker will also represent that owner, purchaser, lessor, or lessee in the purchase, sale, lease, or exchange of real estate, or in exercising an option relating to real estate.


Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-303 Sale agents or associate broker -- Affiliated with principal broker as independent contractors or employees -- Presumption.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-303(1): 
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-303(1)(a): A sales agent or associate broker may be affiliated with a principal broker either as an independent contractor or as an employee.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-303(1)(b): The relationship between sales agent or associate broker and principal broker is presumed to be an independent contractor relationship unless there is clear and convincing evidence that the relationship was intended by the parties to be an employer employee relationship.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-303(2): The presumption of an independent contractor relationship extends to all of the duties and services that the sales agent or associate broker performs, including the preparation and receipt of payment for a broker price opinion.


Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-304 Termination of associate broker or sales agent by principal broker -- Notice.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-304(1): Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act If a principal broker terminates an associate broker or sales agent, the principal broker shall notify the division and the associate broker or sales agent of the termination in a manner prescribed by rule made in accordance with
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-304(2): An associate broker or sales agent may not perform any act under this chapter, directly or indirectly, from and after the effective date of the termination notice until the day on which the associate broker or sales agent is affiliated with a principal broker.
