Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-401 Grounds for disciplinary action.
----------------------------------------------------------------
The following acts are unlawful and grounds for disciplinary action for a person licensed or required to be licensed under this chapter:Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-401(1): 
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-401(1)(a): making a substantial misrepresentation, including in a licensure statement;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-401(1)(b): making an intentional misrepresentation;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-401(1)(c): pursuing a continued and flagrant course of misrepresentation;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-401(1)(d): making a false representation or promise through an agent, sales agent, advertising, or otherwise; or
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-401(1)(e): making a false representation or promise of a character likely to influence, persuade, or induce;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-401(2): acting for more than one party in a transaction without the informed written consent of the parties;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-401(3): 
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-401(3)(a): acting as an associate broker or sales agent while not affiliated with a principal broker;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-401(3)(b): representing or attempting to represent a principal broker other than the principal broker with whom the person is affiliated; or
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-401(3)(c): representing as sales agent or having a contractual relationship similar to that of sales agent with a person other than a principal broker;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-401(4): (4)(a); (4)(a)
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-401(4)(a): failing, within a reasonable time, to account for or to remit money that belongs to another and comes into the person's possession;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-401(4)(b): (4)(a) commingling money described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-401(4)(c): (4)(a) diverting money described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-401(5): Title 16, Chapter 10a, Utah Revised Business Corporation Act; Title 16, Chapter 11, Professional Corporation Act; Title 48, Chapter 3a, Utah Revised Uniform Limited Liability Company Act; 48-3a-1405 paying or offering to pay valuable consideration to a person not licensed under this chapter, except that valuable consideration may be shared:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-401(5)(a): with a principal broker of another jurisdiction; or
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-401(5)(b): Title 16, Chapter 10a, Utah Revised Business Corporation Act; Title 16, Chapter 11, Professional Corporation Act; Title 48, Chapter 3a, Utah Revised Uniform Limited Liability Company Act; 48-3a-1405 as provided under:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-401(5)(b)(i): Title 16, Chapter 10a, Utah Revised Business Corporation Act
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-401(5)(b)(ii): Title 16, Chapter 11, Professional Corporation Act
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-401(5)(b)(iii): Title 48, Chapter 3a, Utah Revised Uniform Limited Liability Company Act; 48-3a-1405
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-401(6): for a principal broker, paying or offering to pay a sales agent or associate broker who is not affiliated with the principal broker at the time the sales agent or associate broker earned the compensation;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-401(7): being incompetent to act as a principal broker, associate broker, or sales agent in such manner as to safeguard the interests of the public;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-401(8): failing to voluntarily furnish a copy of a document to the parties before and after the execution of a document;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-401(9): failing to keep and make available for inspection by the division a record of each transaction, including:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-401(9)(a): the names of buyers and sellers or lessees and lessors;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-401(9)(b): the identification of real estate;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-401(9)(c): the sale or rental price;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-401(9)(d): money received in trust;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-401(9)(e): agreements or instructions from buyers and sellers or lessees and lessors; and
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-401(9)(f): any other information required by rule;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-401(10): failing to disclose, in writing, in the purchase, sale, or rental of real estate, whether the purchase, sale, or rental is made for that person or for an undisclosed principal;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-401(11): regardless of whether the crime is related to the business of real estate:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-401(11)(a): be convicted of:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-401(11)(a)(i): a felony; or
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-401(11)(a)(ii): any of the following involving fraud, misrepresentation, theft, or dishonesty:

Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-401(11)(b)(i): a felony; or

Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-401(11)(b)(ii)(A): a class A misdemeanor;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-401(11)(b)(ii)(B): a class B misdemeanor; or
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-401(11)(b)(ii)(C): a criminal offense comparable to a class A or class B misdemeanor;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-401(11)(c): enter into a plea in abeyance agreement in relation to:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-401(11)(c)(i): a felony; or

Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-402 Investigations -- Disciplinary actions.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-402(1): The division may conduct a public or private investigation within or outside of this state as the division considers necessary to determine whether a person has violated, is violating, or is about to violate this chapter or any rule or order under this chapter.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-402(2): To aid in the enforcement of this chapter or in the prescribing of rules and forms under this chapter, the division may require or permit a person to file a statement in writing, under oath or otherwise as to the facts and circumstances concerning the matter to be investigated.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-402(3): (1) For the purpose of the investigation described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-402(3)(a): administer an oath or affirmation;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-402(3)(b): issue a subpoena that requires:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-402(3)(b)(i): the attendance and testimony of a witness; or
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-402(3)(b)(ii): the production of evidence;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-402(3)(c): take evidence;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-402(3)(d): require the production of a book, paper, contract, record, other document, or information relevant to the investigation; and
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-402(3)(e): serve a subpoena by certified mail.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-402(4): 
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-402(4)(a): A court of competent jurisdiction shall enforce, according to the practice and procedure of the court, a subpoena issued by the division.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-402(4)(b): The division shall pay any witness fee, travel expense, mileage, or any other fee required by the service statutes of the state where the witness or evidence is located.

Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-403 Mishandling of trust money.
-----------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-403(1): 61-2f-404 The division may audit principal brokers' trust accounts or other accounts in which a licensee maintains trust money under this chapter.  If the division's audit shows, in the opinion of the division, gross mismanagement, commingling, or misuse of money, the division, with the concurrence of the commission, may order at the division's expense a complete audit of the account by a certified public accountant, or take other action in accordance with Section
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-403(2): (1); (1) If the commission finds under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-403(3): The licensee may obtain agency review by the executive director or judicial review of any division order.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-403(4): 
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-403(4)(a): If it appears that a person has grossly mismanaged, commingled, or otherwise misused trust money, the division, with or without prior administrative proceedings, may bring an action:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-403(4)(a)(i): in the district court of the district where:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-403(4)(a)(i)(A): the person resides;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-403(4)(a)(i)(B): the person maintains a place of business; or
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-403(4)(a)(i)(C): the act or practice occurred or is about to occur; and
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-403(4)(a)(ii): to enjoin the act or practice and to enforce compliance with this chapter or any rule or order under this chapter.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-403(4)(b): Upon a proper showing, a court shall grant injunctive relief or a temporary restraining order, and may appoint a receiver or conservator.  The division is not required to post a bond in any court proceeding.

Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-405(4): If a person receives money or its equivalent, as commission, compensation, or profit by or in consequence of a violation of this chapter, that person is liable for an additional penalty of not less than the amount of the money received and not more than three times the amount of money received, as may be determined by the court.  This penalty may be sued for in any court of competent jurisdiction, and recovered by any person aggrieved for the person's own use and benefit.

Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-408 Court-ordered discipline.
---------------------------------------------------------
The division shall promptly withhold, suspend, restrict, or reinstate the use of a license issued under this chapter if so ordered by a court.

Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-409 Actions for recovery of compensation restricted.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-409(1): (1)(a)
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-409(1)(a): A person may not bring or maintain an action in any court of this state for the recovery of a commission, fee, or compensation, for any act done or service rendered if the act or service is prohibited under this chapter.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-409(1)(b): (1)(a) Except as provided in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-409(1)(b)(i): a principal broker;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-409(1)(b)(ii): an individual that was licensed as a principal broker at the time the act or service that is the subject of the lawsuit was performed; or
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-409(1)(b)(iii): an entity that, under the records of the Division of Real Estate, is affiliated with a principal broker.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-409(2): 
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-409(2)(a): A sales agent or associate broker may not sue in that individual's own name for the recovery of a fee, commission, or compensation for services as a sales agent or associate broker unless the action is against the principal broker with whom the sales agent or associate broker is or was affiliated.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-409(2)(b): An action for the recovery of a fee, commission, or other compensation may only be instituted and brought by the principal broker with whom a sales agent or associate broker is affiliated.


Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-410 Effect of expiration, revocation, or suspension -- Notice required.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-410(1): (1)(a)
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-410(1)(a): The revocation or suspension of a principal broker license automatically inactivates an associate broker license or a sales agent license that was issued based upon the licensee's affiliation with the principal broker whose license is revoked or suspended, pending a change of principal broker affiliation.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-410(1)(b): (1)(a) If an individual's associate broker license or sales agent license becomes inactive under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-410(2): Before the day on which a suspension or revocation of a principal broker's license is effective, the principal broker shall notify, in writing, each licensee affiliated with the principal broker:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-410(2)(a): that the principal broker's license will be revoked or suspended;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-410(2)(b): of the day on which the revocation or suspension is effective; and
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-410(2)(c): that the licensee's license will be inactive beginning on the day on which the principal broker's license is revoked or suspended.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-410(3): If a principal broker fails to timely renew the principal broker's license in accordance with this chapter, on the day on which the principal broker's license expires, the principal broker shall notify, in writing, each licensee affiliated with the principal broker:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-410(3)(a): that the principal broker's license is expired;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-410(3)(b): of the day on which the principal broker's license expired; and
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-410(3)(c): that the licensee's license is inactive beginning on the day on which the principal broker's license expired.


Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-501 Title.
--------------------------------------
This part is known as the "Real Estate Education, Research, and Recovery Fund Act."

Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-502 Definitions.
--------------------------------------------
For purposes of this part:Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-502(1): "Civil judgment" means a judgment in a civil action that:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-502(1)(a): is awarded in an action brought against a real estate licensee on the basis of fraud, misrepresentation, or deceit in a real estate transaction; and
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-502(1)(b): awards actual damages.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-502(2): "Criminal restitution judgment" means a judgment that, in accordance with the Utah Code of Criminal Procedure, orders criminal restitution to a person and against a real estate licensee for a criminal offense involving fraud, misrepresentation, or deceit in a real estate transaction.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-502(3): "Final judgment" means one of the following judgments upon termination of the proceedings related to the judgment, including appeals:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-502(3)(a): a civil judgment; or
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-502(3)(b): a criminal restitution judgment.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-502(4): 61-2f-503 "Fund" means the Real Estate Education, Research, and Recovery Fund created in Section


Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-503 Real Estate Education, Research, and Recovery Fund.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-503(1): 
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-503(1)(a): There is created an expendable special revenue fund known as the "Real Estate Education, Research, and Recovery Fund."
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-503(1)(b): The actual interest earned on the fund shall be deposited into the fund.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-503(2): 61-2f-505; (1)(b) The money in the fund includes:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-503(2)(a): 61-2f-505 a fee imposed under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-503(2)(b): (1)(b) interest described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-503(3): 61-2f-504 The division shall administer the fund to:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-503(3)(a): reimburse the public for damages caused in a real estate transaction by an individual licensed under this chapter; and
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-503(3)(b): 61-2f-504 in accordance with Section
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-503(3)(b)(i): investigate violations of this chapter related to fraud, misrepresentation, or deceit; or
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-503(3)(b)(ii): provide revenue for improving the real estate profession through education and research with the goal of making licensees more responsible to the public.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-503(4): This part applies to damages caused by an individual licensee.  Reimbursement may not be made for a final judgment against an entity.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-503(5): At the beginning of each fiscal year, the division shall make available $100,000 in the fund to satisfy final judgments rendered against a person licensed under this chapter.


Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-504 Use of money.
---------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-504(1): Money accumulated in the fund in excess of $100,000 shall be set aside and segregated to be used by the division to:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-504(1)(a): investigate violations of this chapter related to fraud, misrepresentation, or deceit; and
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-504(1)(b): advance education and research in the field of real estate.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-504(2): (1); (1) The division may use the money described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-504(2)(a): sponsored by the division;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-504(2)(b): offered by the division in conjunction with any university or college in the state; or
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-504(2)(c): provided for by contracting for a particular research project in the field of real estate for the state.


Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-505 Additional license fee.
-------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-505(1): An individual who applies for or renews a principal broker or associate broker license shall pay, in addition to the application or renewal fee, a reasonable annual fee of up to $18, as determined by the division with the concurrence of the commission.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-505(2): An individual who applies for or renews a sales agent license shall pay in addition to the application or renewal fee a reasonable annual fee of up to $12, as determined by the division with the concurrence of the commission.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-505(3): 13-1-2 Notwithstanding Section


Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-506 Procedure to make a claim against the fund.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-506(1): A person may bring a claim against the fund if:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-506(1)(a): the person obtains a final judgment;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-506(1)(b): the person complies with the requirements under this part;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-506(1)(c): the person is not complicit in the fraud, misrepresentation, or deceit that is the basis of the claim; and
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-506(1)(d): the final judgment that is the basis for the claim:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-506(1)(d)(i): has not been discharged in bankruptcy; and
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-506(1)(d)(ii): when a bankruptcy proceeding is open or commenced during the pendency of the claim, the person obtains an order from the bankruptcy court declaring the final judgment and related debt to be nondischargeable.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-506(2): (1)
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-506(2)(a): A person may not bring a claim against the fund for money owed under a civil judgment unless, within 10 business days of the day on which the person brings the civil action that results in the civil judgment, the person sends to the division a signed notification alleging fraud, misrepresentation, or deceit by a real estate licensee.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-506(2)(b): (1) Within 30 days of the day on which the division receives a notice under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-506(3): (3)(a)(i)
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-506(3)(a): (3)(a)(i) After obtaining a final judgment, to file a claim against the fund, a person shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-506(3)(a)(i): file a verified petition in the court where the final judgment is entered seeking an order directing payment from the fund of an amount equal to the uncollected actual damages owed under the final judgment that are unpaid;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-506(3)(a)(ii): (3)(a)(i) serve a copy of the verified petition described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-506(3)(a)(iii): file a copy of the affidavit of service of the verified petition with the court.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-506(3)(b): Recovery from the fund may not include:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-506(3)(b)(i): punitive damages;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-506(3)(b)(ii): attorney fees;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-506(3)(b)(iii): interest; or
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-506(3)(b)(iv): court costs.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-506(3)(c): Regardless of the number of claimants or parcels of real estate involved in a real estate transaction, the liability of the fund may not exceed:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-506(3)(c)(i): $15,000 for a single transaction; and
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-506(3)(c)(ii): $50,000 for one licensee.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-506(4): (3) A court shall conduct a hearing on a petition filed under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-506(5): (6); (5)(a)(i); (ii) Subject to Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-506(5)(a): (5)(a)(i); (ii) is not:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-506(5)(a)(i): in the case of a civil judgment, the spouse of the judgment debtor;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-506(5)(a)(ii): in the case of a criminal judgment, the spouse of the criminal defendant; or
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-506(5)(a)(iii): (5)(a)(i); (ii) a personal representative of an individual described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-506(5)(b): is in compliance with this chapter;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-506(5)(c): is owed damages under a final judgment that:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-506(5)(c)(i): is issued by the court in the manner prescribed under this section; and
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-506(5)(c)(ii): indicates the amount of the final judgment awarded;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-506(5)(d): has proved the amount still owing on the final judgment on the date the petition is filed;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-506(5)(e): 
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-506(5)(e)(i): 
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-506(5)(e)(i)(A): has had a writ of execution issued upon the final judgment; and
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-506(5)(e)(i)(B): has received a return made by the officer executing the writ showing that no property subject to execution in satisfaction of the final judgment could be found; or
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-506(5)(e)(ii): if execution is levied against the property of the judgment debtor or criminal defendant:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-506(5)(e)(ii)(A): has not realized an amount sufficient to satisfy the final judgment; and
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-506(5)(e)(ii)(B): is owed a specific balance remaining on the final judgment after application of the amount realized;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-506(5)(f): has made reasonable searches and inquiries to ascertain whether the judgment debtor or criminal defendant has any interest in property, real or personal, that may satisfy the final judgment; and
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-506(5)(g): has exercised reasonable diligence to secure payment of the final judgment from the assets of the judgment debtor or criminal defendant.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-506(6): (5); (5)(e); (g) If a person satisfies the court under Subsection


Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-507 Division authority to act upon receipt of petition.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-507(1): 61-2f-506 When the division is served a petition under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-507(1)(a): file an answer to the petition in the court;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-507(1)(b): initiate a review proceeding conducted by the division; or
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-507(1)(c): appear in any proceeding in the name of the defendant to the action or on behalf of the fund.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-507(2): The division may settle a claim against the fund if:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-507(2)(a): the person who brings the claim requests a settlement; and
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-507(2)(b): the court in which the petition is filed approves the settlement.


Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-508 Court determination and order.
--------------------------------------------------------------
If a court determines that the fund should pay a claim under this part, in its order the court shall direct the division to pay from the fund that portion of the final judgment that is payable from the fund in accordance with Section

Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-509 Insufficient funds to satisfy judgments -- Procedure and interest.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
If money deposited in the fund and allotted for satisfying a final judgment against a real estate licensee is insufficient to satisfy an order issued in accordance with SectionUtah Code Annotated § 61-2f-509(1): satisfy the unpaid claims in the order that the unpaid claims are originally filed; and
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-509(2): pay with the claim accumulated interest at the rate of 8% per annum.


Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-510 Division subrogated to claimant -- Authority to revoke license.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-510(1): 
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-510(1)(a): If the division pays a claim against the fund in accordance with this chapter, the division is subrogated to the rights of the person who is paid the claim for the amounts paid out of the fund.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-510(1)(b): The division shall deposit in the fund any amount and interest recovered by the division under this part.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-510(2): (2)(a)
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-510(2)(a): The license of a real estate licensee for whom payment from the fund is made under this chapter shall be automatically revoked.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-510(2)(b): (2)(a) A person whose real estate license is revoked under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-510(2)(b)(i): the amount paid by the fund for a claim that is based on a final judgment against the person; and
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-510(2)(b)(ii): interest at a rate determined by the division with the concurrence of the commission.


Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-511 Authority to take disciplinary action.
----------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-511(1): This part does not limit the authority of the director of the division to take disciplinary action against a real estate licensee for a violation of this chapter or of the rules of the commission and division.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-511(2): A real estate licensee's payment of all the obligations of the real estate licensee to the fund does not nullify or modify the effect of any other disciplinary proceeding brought pursuant to this chapter or the rules of the commission.


Utah Code Annotated § 61-2f-512 Failure to comply with provisions constitutes a waiver.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
A person's failure to comply with this part constitutes a waiver of any right under this part.

Utah Code Annotated - Title 61 - Chapter 2g - Real Estate Appraiser Licensing and Certification Act
***************************************************************************************************

Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-101 Title.
--------------------------------------
This chapter is known as the "Real Estate Appraiser Licensing and Certification Act."

Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-102 Definitions.
--------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-102(1): (1)(a)(ii); 61-2g-204 As used in this chapter:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-102(1)(a): 
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-102(1)(a)(i): "Appraisal" means an analysis, opinion, or conclusion relating to the nature, quality, value, or utility of a specified interest in, or aspect of, identified real estate or identified real property.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-102(1)(a)(ii): An appraisal is classified by the nature of the assignment as a valuation appraisal, an analysis assignment, or a review assignment in accordance with the following definitions:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-102(1)(a)(ii)(A): "Analysis assignment" means an unbiased analysis, opinion, or conclusion that relates to the nature, quality, or utility of identified real estate or identified real property.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-102(1)(a)(ii)(B): "Review assignment" means an unbiased analysis, opinion, or conclusion that forms an opinion as to the adequacy and appropriateness of a valuation appraisal or an analysis assignment.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-102(1)(a)(ii)(C): "Valuation appraisal" means an unbiased analysis, opinion, or conclusion that estimates the value of an identified parcel of real estate or identified real property at a particular point in time.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-102(1)(b): "Appraisal Foundation" means the Appraisal Foundation that was incorporated as an Illinois not-for-profit corporation on November 30, 1987.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-102(1)(c): (1)(a)(ii)
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-102(1)(c)(i): "Appraisal report" means a communication, written or oral, of an appraisal.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-102(1)(c)(ii): (1)(a)(ii) An appraisal report is classified by the nature of the assignment as a valuation report, analysis report, or review report in accordance with the definitions provided in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-102(1)(c)(iii): The testimony of a person relating to the person's analyses, conclusions, or opinions concerning identified real estate or identified real property is considered to be an oral appraisal report.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-102(1)(d): "Appraisal Qualification Board" means the Appraisal Qualification Board of the Appraisal Foundation.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-102(1)(e): 61-2g-204 "Board" means the Real Estate Appraiser Licensing and Certification Board that is established in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-102(1)(f): "Certified appraisal report" means a written or oral appraisal report that is certified by a state-certified general appraiser or state-certified residential appraiser.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-102(1)(g): "Concurrence" means that the entities that are given a concurring role jointly agree to an action.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-102(1)(h): 
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-102(1)(h)(i): 
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-102(1)(h)(i)(A): "Consultation service" means an engagement to provide a real estate valuation service analysis, opinion, conclusion, or other service that does not fall within the definition of appraisal.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-102(1)(h)(i)(B): "Consultation service" does not mean a valuation appraisal, analysis assignment, or review assignment.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-102(1)(h)(ii): Regardless of the intention of the client or employer, if a person prepares an unbiased analysis, opinion, or conclusion, the analysis, opinion, or conclusion is considered to be an appraisal and not a consultation service.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-102(1)(i): "Contingent fee" means a fee or other form of compensation, payment of which is dependent on or conditioned by:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-102(1)(i)(i): the reporting of a predetermined analysis, opinion, or conclusion by the person performing the analysis, opinion, or conclusion; or
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-102(1)(i)(ii): achieving a result specified by the person requesting the analysis, opinion, or conclusion.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-102(1)(j): "Credential" means a state-issued registration, license, or certification that allows an individual to perform any act or service that requires licensure or certification under this chapter.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-102(1)(k): "Division" means the Division of Real Estate of the Department of Commerce.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-102(1)(l): "Evaluation" means an opinion on the market value of real property or real estate that:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-102(1)(l)(i): is made in accordance with the Interagency Appraisal and Evaluation Guidelines; and
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-102(1)(l)(ii): is provided to a financial institution for use in a real estate related transaction for which the regulations of the federal financial institutions regulatory agencies do not require an appraisal.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-102(1)(m): "Executive director" means the executive director of the Department of Commerce.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-102(1)(n): "Federal financial institutions regulatory agencies" means:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-102(1)(n)(i): the Board of Governors of the Federal Reserve System;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-102(1)(n)(ii): the Federal Deposit Insurance Corporation;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-102(1)(n)(iii): the Office of the Comptroller of the Currency; and
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-102(1)(n)(iv): the National Credit Union Administration.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-102(1)(o): "Federally related transaction" means a real estate related transaction that is required by federal law or by federal regulation to be supported by an appraisal prepared by:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-102(1)(o)(i): a state-licensed appraiser; or
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-102(1)(o)(ii): a state-certified appraiser.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-102(1)(p): "Financial institution" means an insured:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-102(1)(p)(i): depository as defined in 12 U.S.C. Sec. 1813(c)(1); or
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-102(1)(p)(ii): credit union as defined in 12 U.S.C. Sec. 1752(7).
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-102(1)(q): "Interagency Appraisal and Evaluation Guidelines" means the guidelines published as Interagency Appraisal and Evaluation Guidelines, 75 Fed. Reg. 77,450 (Dec. 10, 2010), and all amendments or updates thereto.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-102(1)(r): "Real estate" means an identified parcel or tract of land including improvements if any.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-102(1)(s): "Real estate appraisal activity" means the act or process of making an appraisal of real estate or real property and preparing an appraisal report.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-102(1)(t): "Real estate related transaction" means:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-102(1)(t)(i): the sale, lease, purchase, investment in, or exchange of real property or an interest in real property, or the financing of such a transaction;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-102(1)(t)(ii): the refinancing of real property or an interest in real property; or
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-102(1)(t)(iii): the use of real property or an interest in real property as security for a loan or investment, including mortgage-backed securities.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-102(1)(u): "Real property" means one or more defined interests, benefits, or rights inherent in the ownership of real estate.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-102(1)(v): "State-certified general appraiser" means a person who holds a current, valid certification as a state-certified general appraiser issued under this chapter.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-102(1)(w): "State-certified residential appraiser" means a person who holds a current, valid certification as a state-certified residential real estate appraiser issued under this chapter.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-102(1)(x): "State-licensed appraiser" means a person who holds a current, valid license as a state-licensed appraiser issued under this chapter.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-102(1)(y): "Trainee" means an individual who:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-102(1)(y)(i): does not hold an appraiser license or appraiser certification issued under this chapter;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-102(1)(y)(ii): works under the direct supervision of a state-certified appraiser to earn experience for licensure; and
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-102(1)(y)(iii): is registered as a trainee under this chapter.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-102(1)(z): "Unbiased analysis, opinion, or conclusion" means an analysis, opinion, or conclusion relating to the nature, quality, value, or utility of identified real estate or identified real property that is prepared by a person who is employed or retained to act, or would be perceived by third parties or the public as acting, as a disinterested third-party in rendering the analysis, opinion, or conclusion.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-102(2): Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-102(2)(a): Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act If a term not defined in this section is defined by rule, the term shall have the meaning established by the division by rule made in accordance with
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-102(2)(b): If a term not defined in this section is not defined by rule, the term shall have the meaning commonly accepted in the business community.


Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-103 Other law unaffected.
-----------------------------------------------------
This chapter may not be considered to prohibit a person licensed, certified, or registered under this chapter from engaging in the practice of real estate appraising as a professional corporation or a limited liability company in accordance with:Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-103(1): Title 16, Chapter 11, Professional Corporation Act
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-103(2): Title 48, Chapter 3a, Utah Revised Uniform Limited Liability Company Act


Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-201 Duties and powers of division in general.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-201(1): The division shall administer and enforce this chapter.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-201(2): 61-2g-403; Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act; (2)(k) The division has the following powers and duties:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-201(2)(a): The division shall:

Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-201(2)(a)(iii): issue a license or certification to a qualified applicant pursuant to this chapter; and
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-201(2)(a)(iv): register an individual who applies and qualifies for registration as a trainee under this chapter.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-201(2)(b): The division shall hold public hearings under the direction of the board.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-201(2)(c): The division may:

Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-201(2)(c)(ii): administer or contract for the administration of licensing and certification examinations as may be required to carry out the division's responsibilities under this chapter.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-201(2)(d): The division shall provide administrative assistance to the board by providing to the board the facilities, equipment, supplies, and personnel that are required to enable the board to carry out the board's responsibilities under this chapter.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-201(2)(e): The division shall assist the board in improving the quality of the continuing education available to a person licensed, certified, or registered under this chapter.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-201(2)(f): 61-2g-403 The division shall assist the board with respect to the proper interpretation or explanation of the Uniform Standards of Professional Appraisal Practice as required by Section
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-201(2)(g): The division may:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-201(2)(g)(i): promote research and conduct studies relating to the profession of real estate appraising; and
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-201(2)(g)(ii): sponsor real estate appraisal educational activities.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-201(2)(h): Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act The division shall adopt, with the concurrence of the board, rules for the administration of this chapter pursuant to
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-201(2)(i): The division shall employ an appropriate staff to investigate allegations that a person required to be licensed, certified, or registered under this chapter fails to comply with this chapter.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-201(2)(j): The division may employ other professional, clerical, and technical staff as may be necessary to properly administer the work of the division under this chapter.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-201(2)(k): (2)(k)
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-201(2)(k)(i): Upon request, the division shall make available, either directly or through a third-party, a list of the names and addresses of the persons licensed, registered, or certified by the division under this chapter.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-201(2)(k)(ii): (2)(k) A person who requests a list under this Subsection

Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-202 Division service fees -- Federal registry fees.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-202(1): 63J-1-504 The division, with the concurrence of the board, shall establish and collect fees in accordance with Section
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-202(2): The division shall collect the annual registry fee established by the Federal Financial Institutions Examinations Council from those certificate holders who seek to perform appraisals in federally related transactions.  The division shall transmit the fees to the federal Appraisal Subcommittee at least annually.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-202(3): If a person pays a fee or costs to the division with a negotiable instrument or any other payment method that is not honored:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-202(3)(a): the transaction for which the payment is submitted is voidable by the division;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-202(3)(b): the division may reverse the transaction if payment of the applicable fee or costs is not received in full; and
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-202(3)(c): the person's license, certification, or registration is automatically suspended:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-202(3)(c)(i): beginning the day on which the payment is due; and
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-202(3)(c)(ii): ending the day on which payment is made in full.


Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-203 Division to publish roster of appraisers.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-203(1): The division shall prepare and issue at least once each calendar year a roster of appraisers containing the information required by the Federal Financial Institutions Examination Council.  The division shall transmit the roster to the Federal Financial Institutions Examinations Council at least annually.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-203(2): 63J-1-504 The division may, upon payment of a fee established by the division in accordance with Section
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-203(2)(a): licensed, certified, or registered under this chapter; or
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-203(2)(b): previously registered, licensed, or certified under this chapter.


Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-204 Real Estate Appraiser Licensing and Certification Board.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-204(1): Chapter 2e, Appraisal Management Company Registration and Regulation Act; Chapter 2c, Utah Residential Mortgage Practices and Licensing Act; 70D-2-102; Title 70D, Chapter 2, Mortgage Lending and Servicing Act; Title 63G, Chapter 24, Part 2, Vacancies
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-204(1)(a): Chapter 2e, Appraisal Management Company Registration and Regulation Act; Chapter 2c, Utah Residential Mortgage Practices and Licensing Act; 70D-2-102; Title 70D, Chapter 2, Mortgage Lending and Servicing Act There is established a Real Estate Appraiser Licensing and Certification Board that consists of seven regular members as follows:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-204(1)(a)(i): one state-licensed or state-certified appraiser who may be either a residential or general licensee or certificate holder;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-204(1)(a)(ii): one state-certified residential appraiser;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-204(1)(a)(iii): one state-certified general appraiser;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-204(1)(a)(iv): one member who is certified as either a state-certified residential appraiser or a state-certified general appraiser;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-204(1)(a)(v): Chapter 2e, Appraisal Management Company Registration and Regulation Act one member who represents an appraisal management company registered in accordance with
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-204(1)(a)(vi): Chapter 2c, Utah Residential Mortgage Practices and Licensing Act; 70D-2-102; Title 70D, Chapter 2, Mortgage Lending and Servicing Act one member:

Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-306(3): (3)(a)(ii) A person who is licensed, certified, or registered under this chapter shall notify the division of the following by sending the division a signed statement within 10 business days of:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-306(3)(a): a conviction of, or the entry of a plea in abeyance to:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-306(3)(a)(i): a felony; or
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-306(3)(a)(ii): a misdemeanor involving financial services or a financial services-related business, fraud, a false statement or omission, theft or wrongful taking of property, bribery, perjury, forgery, counterfeiting, or extortion;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-306(3)(b): (3)(a)(ii) the potential resolution of a felony or of a misdemeanor described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-306(3)(b)(i): a diversion agreement; or
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-306(3)(b)(ii): any other agreement under which a criminal charge is suspended for a period of time;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-306(3)(c): the suspension, revocation, surrender, cancellation, or denial of a professional license, certification, or registration of the person, whether the license, certification, or registration is issued by this state or another jurisdiction; or
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-306(3)(d): the entry of a cease and desist order or a temporary or permanent injunction:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-306(3)(d)(i): against the person by a court or administrative agency; and

Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-307 Continuing education requirements.
------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-307(1): As a prerequisite to renewal of a license, certification, or registration, the applicant for renewal shall present evidence satisfactory to the division of having met the continuing education requirements of this section.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-307(2): A person licensed, certified, or registered under this chapter shall complete during the two-year period immediately preceding the filing of an application for renewal not less than 28 classroom hours of instruction in courses or seminars that have received the approval of the division.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-307(3): (3)
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-307(3)(a): The division, with the concurrence of the board, may adopt rules for the implementation of this section to assure that a person renewing that person's license, certification, or registration under this chapter has a working knowledge of current real estate appraisal theories, practices, and techniques that will enable the person to provide competent real estate appraisal services to the members of the public with whom that person deals in a professional relationship under the authority of that person's license, certificate, or registration.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-307(3)(b): An amendment or repeal of a rule adopted by the division under this section, with the concurrence of the board, does not operate to deprive a person of credit toward renewal of that person's license, certification, or registration for a course of instruction that is successfully completed by the applicant before the date of the amendment or repeal of the rule.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-307(3)(c): (3) The rules made under this Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-307(3)(c)(i): policies and procedures to be followed in obtaining division approval of courses of instruction and seminars;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-307(3)(c)(ii): standards, policies, and procedures to be used by the division in evaluating an applicant's claims of equivalency; and
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-307(3)(c)(iii): standards, monitoring methods, and systems for recording attendance to be employed by course and seminar sponsors as a prerequisite to division approval of courses and seminars for credit.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-307(4): (2) In lieu of meeting the requirements set forth in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-307(4)(a): completion of an educational program of study determined by the board to be equivalent, for continuing education purposes, to courses or seminars approved by the board; or
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-307(4)(b): participation other than as a student in educational processes and programs approved by the board that relate to real property appraisal theory, practices, or techniques including teaching, program development, and preparation of textbooks, monographs, articles, and other instructional materials.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-307(5): A person whose license, certification, or registration is suspended as the result of a disciplinary action taken under this chapter may not apply for reinstatement unless the person presents evidence of completion of the continuing education requirement that is required by this chapter for renewal.

Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-310 Reciprocal licensure.
-----------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-310(1): An applicant for licensure or certification in this state who is credentialed under the laws of any other state, territory, or district may obtain a reciprocal credential in this state if:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-310(1)(a): the individual holds a current, valid credential issued by a state that, on the day on which the individual submits an application, is in compliance with Title XI of the Financial Institutions Reform, Recovery and Enforcement Act of 1989, as determined by the Appraisal Subcommittee of the Federal Financial Institutions Examination Council; and
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-310(1)(b): the credentialing requirements of that state, that are in force on the day on which the individual submits an application, meet or exceed the credentialing requirements described in this chapter and the rules made under this chapter.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-310(2): (1) An individual who holds a reciprocal credential described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-310(2)(a): the payment of fees; and
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-310(2)(b): continuing education.


Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-311 State-licensed appraiser -- Authority and qualifications.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-311(1): A state-licensed appraiser is authorized to appraise complex and noncomplex 1-4 family residential units in this state having a transaction value permitted under the Financial Institutions Reform, Recovery, and Enforcement Act of 1989, and related federal regulations.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-311(2): A state-licensed appraiser is authorized to appraise vacant or unimproved land having a transaction value permitted under the Financial Institutions Reform, Recovery, and Enforcement Act of 1989, and related federal regulations that is utilized for 1-4 family purposes or for which the highest and best use is 1-4 family purposes and subdivisions for which a development analysis/appraisal is not necessary.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-311(3): A state-licensed appraiser may not issue a certified appraisal report.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-311(4): (5); (5) To qualify as a state-licensed appraiser, an applicant must:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-311(4)(a): be of good moral character;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-311(4)(b): demonstrate honesty, competency, integrity, truthfulness, and general fitness to command the confidence of the community;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-311(4)(c): pass the licensing examination with a satisfactory score as determined by the Appraisal Qualification Board;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-311(4)(d): (5) successfully complete the educational requirements established by rule in accordance with Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-311(4)(e): (5) possess the experience in real property appraisal established by rule in accordance with Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-311(5): Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act; (4)(d); (4)(e); (5)(a)
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-311(5)(a): Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act; (4)(d); (4)(e) The division shall, with the concurrence of the board, make rules in accordance with
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-311(5)(a)(i): (4)(d) the educational requirements described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-311(5)(a)(ii): (4)(e) the experience in real property appraisal described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-311(5)(b): (5)(a) The educational and experience requirements established under Subsection


Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-312 State-certified appraisers -- Authority.
------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-312(1): A state-certified residential appraiser:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-312(1)(a): is authorized to appraise the types of real estate that a state-licensed appraiser is authorized to appraise;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-312(1)(b): is authorized to appraise 1-4 unit residential real estate without regard to transaction value or complexity; and
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-312(1)(c): is not authorized to appraise subdivisions for which a development analysis/appraisal is necessary.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-312(2): A state-certified general appraiser is authorized to appraise all types of real estate and real property.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-312(3): A state-certified appraiser who satisfies all requirements described in this chapter and in rule made under this chapter may supervise trainees as allowed by rule.

Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-315(3):

Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-315(3)(b): Upon a suspension or revocation of a license, certification, or registration under this chapter, the individual holding the applicable document shall immediately return the document to the division.

Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-402 Principal place of business -- Display of documents -- Notify of changes -- Nonresidents.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-402(1): A person licensed or certified under this chapter shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-402(1)(a): designate and maintain a principal place of business; and
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-402(1)(b): conspicuously display the person's license or certification.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-402(2): Upon a change of a person's principal business location or home address, a person licensed or certified under this chapter shall promptly send the division a signed statement notifying the division of the change within 10 business days of the change.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-402(3): A nonresident licensee or certificate holder is not required to maintain a place of business in this state if the nonresident maintains an active place of business in the nonresident's state of domicile.

Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-404 Registration, licensure, or certification prerequisite to suit for compensation.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
A person engaged in the business of real estate appraising in this state or acting in the capacity of a real estate appraiser in this state may not bring or maintain an action as a plaintiff in a court of this state to collect compensation for the performance of real estate appraisal services for which registration, licensure, or certification is required by this chapter without alleging and proving that the person was the holder of a valid registration, license, or certification in this state at all times during the performance of the real estate appraisal services.

Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-405 Recordkeeping requirements.
-----------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-405(1): (2) Subject to Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-405(1)(a): each written contract engaging the person's services for real estate or real property appraisal work;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-405(1)(b): each appraisal report prepared or signed by the person; and
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-405(1)(c): the supporting data assembled and formulated by the appraiser in preparing each appraisal report.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-405(2): The five-year period for retention of records is applicable to each engagement of the services of the appraiser and begins upon the date of the delivery of each appraisal report to the client unless, within the five-year period, the appraiser is notified that the appraisal or the appraisal report is involved in litigation, in which event the records must be maintained for the longer of:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-405(2)(a): five years; or
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-405(2)(b): two years following the date of the final disposition of the litigation.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-405(3): Upon reasonable notice, a person licensed or certified under this chapter shall make the records required to be maintained under this chapter available to the division for inspection and copying.


Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-406 Contingent fees.
------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-406(1): A person licensed or certified under this chapter who enters into an agreement to perform an appraisal may not accept a contingent fee.

Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-406(2)(a): 59-2-1017 if the person is not licensed or certified under this chapter, presents or provides a price estimate or property tax information in accordance with Section
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-406(2)(b): if the person is licensed or certified under this chapter, enters into an agreement to provide consultation services.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-406(3): (2) A person that accepts payment of a fee under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-406(3)(a): clearly state in each oral statement the fact that the person is accepting payment of a fee under a contingent fee arrangement and whether the person is licensed or certified under this chapter; and
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-406(3)(b): clearly state in any written consultation report or summary, letter of transmittal, certification statement, price estimate, or property tax information that the document is prepared under a contingent fee arrangement and whether the person is licensed or certified under this chapter.

Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-501 Enforcement -- Investigation -- Orders -- Hearings.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-501(1): (1)(a); Title 63G, Chapter 4, Administrative Procedures Act; (3)
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-501(1)(a): The division may conduct a public or private investigation of the actions of:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-501(1)(a)(i): a person registered, licensed, or certified under this chapter;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-501(1)(a)(ii): an applicant for registration, licensure, or certification;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-501(1)(a)(iii): an applicant for renewal of registration, licensure, or certification; or
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-501(1)(a)(iv): a person required to be registered, licensed, or certified under this chapter.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-501(1)(b): (1)(a); Title 63G, Chapter 4, Administrative Procedures Act; (3) The division may initiate an agency action against a person described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-501(1)(b)(i): impose disciplinary action;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-501(1)(b)(ii): deny issuance to an applicant of:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-501(1)(b)(ii)(A): an original registration, license, or certification; or
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-501(1)(b)(ii)(B): a renewal of a registration, license, or certification; or
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-501(1)(b)(iii): (3) issue a cease and desist order as provided in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-501(2): (1); (2)(e)(i)
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-501(2)(a): (1) The division may:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-501(2)(a)(i): administer an oath or affirmation;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-501(2)(a)(ii): issue a subpoena that requires:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-501(2)(a)(ii)(A): the attendance and testimony of a witness; or
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-501(2)(a)(ii)(B): the production of evidence;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-501(2)(a)(iii): take evidence; and
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-501(2)(a)(iv): (1) require the production of a book, paper, contract, record, document, information, or evidence relevant to the investigation described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-501(2)(b): The division may serve a subpoena by certified mail.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-501(2)(c): A failure to respond to a request by the division in an investigation authorized under this chapter within 10 days after the day on which the request is served is considered to be a separate violation of this chapter, including:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-501(2)(c)(i): failing to respond to a subpoena as a witness;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-501(2)(c)(ii): withholding evidence; or
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-501(2)(c)(iii): failing to produce a book, paper, contract, document, information, or record.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-501(2)(d): 
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-501(2)(d)(i): A court of competent jurisdiction shall enforce, according to the practice and procedure of the court, a subpoena issued by the division.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-501(2)(d)(ii): The division shall pay any witness fee, travel expense, mileage, or any other fee required by the service statutes of the state where the witness or evidence is located.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-501(2)(e): (2)(e)(i)
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-501(2)(e)(i): If a person is found to have violated this chapter or a rule made under this chapter, the person shall pay the costs incurred by the division to copy a book, paper, contract, document, information, or record required under this chapter, including the costs incurred to copy an electronic book, paper, contract, document, information, or record in a universally readable format.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-501(2)(e)(ii): (2)(e)(i) If a person fails to pay the costs described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-501(2)(e)(ii)(A): beginning the day on which the payment of costs is due; and
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-501(2)(e)(ii)(B): ending the day on which the costs are paid.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-501(3): (3)(b); Title 63G, Chapter 4, Administrative Procedures Act
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-501(3)(a): The director shall issue and serve upon a person an order directing that person to cease and desist from an act if:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-501(3)(a)(i): the director has reason to believe that the person has been engaging, is about to engage, or is engaging in the act constituting a violation of this chapter; and
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-501(3)(a)(ii): it appears to the director that it would be in the public interest to stop the act.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-501(3)(b): Within 10 days after the day on which the order is served, the person upon whom the order is served may request a hearing.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-501(3)(c): (3)(b) Pending a hearing requested under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-501(3)(d): Title 63G, Chapter 4, Administrative Procedures Act If a request for hearing is made, the division shall follow the procedures and requirements of
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-501(4): (3); 61-2g-502; (3); (3); (3); (3)
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-501(4)(a): (3); 61-2g-502 After a hearing requested under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-501(4)(a)(i): shall issue an order making the cease and desist order permanent; and
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-501(4)(a)(ii): 61-2g-502 may impose another disciplinary action under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-501(4)(b): (3); (3); (3); (3) The director shall commence an action in the name of the Department of Commerce and Division of Real Estate, in the district court in the county in which an act described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-501(4)(b)(i): (3); (3)
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-501(4)(b)(i)(A): (3) a hearing is not requested under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-501(4)(b)(i)(B): (3) the individual fails to cease the act described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-501(4)(b)(ii): (3) after discontinuing the act described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-501(5): A remedy or action provided in this section does not limit, interfere with, or prevent the prosecution of another remedy or action, including a criminal proceeding.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-501(6): (6)(b); (6)(a); (6)(a)
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-501(6)(a): (6)(b) Except as provided in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-501(6)(a)(i): four years after the day on which the violation is reported to the division; or
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-501(6)(a)(ii): 10 years after the day on which the violation occurred.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-501(6)(b): (6)(a); (6)(a) The division may commence a disciplinary action under this chapter after the time period described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-501(6)(b)(i): 
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-501(6)(b)(i)(A): the disciplinary action is in response to a civil or criminal judgment or settlement; and
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-501(6)(b)(i)(B): the division initiates the disciplinary action no later than one year after the day on which the judgment is issued or the settlement is final; or
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-501(6)(b)(ii): (6)(a) the division and the individual subject to a disciplinary action enter into a written stipulation to extend the time period described in Subsection

Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-502 Disciplinary action -- Grounds.
---------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-502(1): (2); (1)(b)(i); (vii); (1)(b)(i); (viii); Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act; Title 63A, Chapter 3, Part 5, Office of State Debt Collection
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-502(1)(a): The board may order disciplinary action, with the concurrence of the division, against a person:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-502(1)(a)(i): registered, licensed, or certified under this chapter; or
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-502(1)(a)(ii): required to be registered, licensed, or certified under this chapter.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-502(1)(b): (2); (1)(b)(i); (vii); (1)(b)(i); (viii) On the basis of a ground listed in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-502(1)(b)(i): revoking, suspending, or placing a person's registration, license, or certification on probation;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-502(1)(b)(ii): denying a person's original registration, license, or certification;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-502(1)(b)(iii): denying a person's renewal license, certification, or registration;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-502(1)(b)(iv): in the case of denial or revocation of a registration, license, or certification, setting a waiting period for an applicant to apply for a registration, license, or certification under this chapter;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-502(1)(b)(v): ordering remedial education;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-502(1)(b)(vi): imposing a civil penalty upon a person not to exceed the greater of:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-502(1)(b)(vi)(A): $5,000 for each violation; or
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-502(1)(b)(vi)(B): the amount of any gain or economic benefit from a violation;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-502(1)(b)(vii): issuing a cease and desist order;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-502(1)(b)(viii): (1)(b)(i); (vii) modifying an action described in Subsections
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-502(1)(b)(ix): (1)(b)(i); (viii) doing any combination of Subsections
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-502(1)(c): Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act; Title 63A, Chapter 3, Part 5, Office of State Debt Collection
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-502(1)(c)(i): If the board or division issues an order that orders a fine or educational requirements as part of the disciplinary action against a person, including a stipulation and order, the board or division shall state in the order the deadline by which the person shall comply with the fine or educational requirements.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-502(1)(c)(ii): Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act; Title 63A, Chapter 3, Part 5, Office of State Debt Collection If a person fails to comply with a stated deadline:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-502(1)(c)(ii)(A): the person's license, certificate, or registration is automatically suspended:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-502(1)(c)(ii)(A)(I): beginning on the day specified in the order as the deadline for compliance; and
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-502(1)(c)(ii)(A)(II): ending the day on which the person complies in full with the order; and
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-502(1)(c)(ii)(B): Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act; Title 63A, Chapter 3, Part 5, Office of State Debt Collection if the person fails to pay a fine required by an order, the division may begin a collection process:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-502(1)(c)(ii)(B)(I): Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act established by the division by rule made in accordance with
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-502(1)(c)(ii)(B)(II): Title 63A, Chapter 3, Part 5, Office of State Debt Collection subject to
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-502(2): 31A-2-402; 31A-2-405; 31A-2-405(2) The following are grounds for disciplinary action under this section:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-502(2)(a): procuring or attempting to procure a registration, license, or certification under this chapter:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-502(2)(a)(i): by fraud; or
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-502(2)(a)(ii): by making a false statement, submitting false information, or making a material misrepresentation in an application filed with the division;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-502(2)(b): paying money or attempting to pay money other than a fee provided for by this chapter to a member or employee of the division to procure a registration, license, or certification under this chapter;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-502(2)(c): an act or omission in the practice of real estate appraising that constitutes dishonesty, fraud, or misrepresentation;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-502(2)(d): entry of a judgment against a registrant, licensee, or certificate holder on grounds of fraud, misrepresentation, or deceit in the making of an appraisal of real estate;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-502(2)(e): regardless of whether the crime is related to the appraisal business, to:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-502(2)(e)(i): be convicted of a felony;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-502(2)(e)(ii): be convicted of any of the following involving fraud, misrepresentation, theft, or dishonesty:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-502(2)(e)(ii)(A): a class A misdemeanor:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-502(2)(e)(ii)(B): a class B misdemeanor; or
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-502(2)(e)(ii)(C): a criminal offense comparable to a class A or class B misdemeanor;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-502(2)(e)(iii): plead guilty or nolo contendere to a felony;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-502(2)(e)(iv): plead guilty or nolo contendere to any of the following involving fraud, misrepresentation, theft, or dishonesty:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-502(2)(e)(iv)(A): a class A misdemeanor:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-502(2)(e)(iv)(B): a class B misdemeanor; or
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-502(2)(e)(iv)(C): a criminal offense comparable to a class A or class B misdemeanor;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-502(2)(e)(v): enter into a plea in abeyance agreement involving a felony; or
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-502(2)(e)(vi): enter into a plea in abeyance agreement involving any of the following involving fraud, misrepresentation, theft, or dishonesty:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-502(2)(e)(vi)(A): a class A misdemeanor:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-502(2)(e)(vi)(B): a class B misdemeanor; or
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-502(2)(e)(vi)(C): a criminal offense comparable to a class A or class B misdemeanor;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-502(2)(f): engaging in the business of real estate appraising under an assumed or fictitious name not properly registered in this state;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-502(2)(g): paying a finder's fee or a referral fee to a person not licensed or certified under this chapter in connection with an appraisal of real estate or real property in this state;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-502(2)(h): making a false or misleading statement in:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-502(2)(h)(i): that portion of a written appraisal report that deals with professional qualifications; or
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-502(2)(h)(ii): testimony concerning professional qualifications;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-502(2)(i): violating or disregarding:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-502(2)(i)(i): this chapter;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-502(2)(i)(ii): an order of:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-502(2)(i)(ii)(A): the board; or
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-502(2)(i)(ii)(B): the division, in a case when the board delegates to the division the authority to make a decision on behalf of the board; or
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-502(2)(i)(iii): a rule issued under this chapter;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-502(2)(j): violating the confidential nature of governmental records to which a person registered, licensed, or certified under this chapter gained access through employment or engagement as an appraiser by a governmental agency;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-502(2)(k): accepting a contingent fee for performing an appraisal if in fact the fee is or was contingent upon:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-502(2)(k)(i): the appraiser reporting a predetermined analysis, opinion, or conclusion;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-502(2)(k)(ii): the analysis, opinion, conclusion, or valuation reached; or
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-502(2)(k)(iii): the consequences resulting from the appraisal assignment;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-502(2)(l): unprofessional conduct as defined by statute or rule;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-502(2)(m): 31A-2-402; 31A-2-405; 31A-2-405(2) in the case of a dual licensed title licensee as defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-502(2)(m)(i): 31A-2-405 providing a title insurance product or service without the approval required by Section
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-502(2)(m)(ii): 31A-2-405(2) knowingly providing false or misleading information in the statement required by Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-502(2)(n): other conduct that constitutes dishonest dealing.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-502(3): A person previously licensed, certified, or registered under this chapter remains responsible for, and is subject to disciplinary action for, an act that the person committed, while the person was licensed, certified, or registered, in violation of this chapter or an administrative rule in effect at the time that the person committed the act, regardless of whether the person is currently licensed, certified, or registered.


Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-503 Reinstatement of license, certification, and registration.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-503(1): (2) An individual whose license, certification, or registration is revoked under this chapter:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-503(1)(a): may not apply for renewal or reinstatement of that license, certification, or registration; and
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-503(1)(b): (2) may apply for licensure, certification, or registration as prescribed for an original license, certification, or registration subject to the limitations in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-503(2): (1) An applicant for licensure, certification, or registration under Subsection


Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-504 Disciplinary hearing process.
-------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-504(1): Title 63G, Chapter 4, Administrative Procedures Act The division and board shall comply with
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-504(2): Before disciplinary action may be taken under this chapter, the division shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-504(2)(a): notify the person against whom disciplinary action is sought; and
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-504(2)(b): commence an adjudicative proceeding.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-504(3): (2); 61-2g-502 If, after the hearing, the board determines, with the concurrence of the division, that a person described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-504(4): 
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-504(4)(a): The board may:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-504(4)(a)(i): conduct hearings with the assistance of an administrative law judge; or
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-504(4)(a)(ii): delegate hearings to an administrative law judge.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-504(4)(b): If a hearing is delegated by the board to an administrative law judge, the administrative law judge shall submit to the board and the director for their consideration:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-504(4)(b)(i): written findings of fact;
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-504(4)(b)(ii): written conclusions of law; and
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-504(4)(b)(iii): a recommended order.
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-504(5): Title 78B, Chapter 8, Part 5, Small Business Equal Access to Justice Act
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-504(5)(a): An applicant, licensee, certificate holder, registrant, or person aggrieved, including the complainant, may obtain judicial review of an adverse ruling, order, or decision.

Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-505 Penalty for violating this chapter -- Automatic revocation.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-505(1): In addition to being subject to a disciplinary action, a person required to be licensed, certified, or registered under this chapter who violates this chapter:
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-505(1)(a): is guilty of a class A misdemeanor, upon a conviction of a first violation of this chapter; and
Utah Code Annotated § 61-2g-505(1)(b): is guilty of a third degree felony, upon conviction of a second or subsequent violation of this chapter.
